  - **Pivot**: if the recurring dogfood produces noise (false-positive findings > 3 per month), tighten the finding-detection gate — require the same signal across 2 consecutive weekly runs before filing. Decision boundary: > 3 false-positive recurring-dogfood-filed PRs in 30 days.
  - **Acceptance**: the workflow exists, runs on cron, produces an artifact + a draft PR on new findings; RECURRING.md documents the cadence + result schema.
  - **Anchor**: Forsgren, N., Humble, J., Kim, G., *Accelerate: The Science of Lean Software and DevOps*, IT Revolution Press, 2018, ISBN 978-1942788331 (continuous verification — observers run on a regular cadence, not just operator-initiated); Beyer, B., et al., *Site Reliability Engineering*, O'Reilly, 2016, ISBN 978-1491929124 (canary + dogfood discipline — the observer-on-self IS the canary); rule #9 (vision.md § 9 — pre-registered HDD; this task declares the finding-rate metric). Surfaced-by observer dogfood, 2026-05-12T02:52Z (2 findings on first run → expected steady-state at ≥ 0.5 findings / week is a reasonable forecast).
  - **Risk**: low. Recurring task; the workflow's blast radius is one PR if findings exceed 0.
  - **Surfaced-by**: observer dogfood, 2026-05-12T02:52Z. The 2-finding-per-first-run rate is the underlying evidence.

- [ ] `observer-skill-protocol-versioning` — `skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md` carries an explicit `protocol_version: <N>` so observer-filed PRs cite the version they were filed under
  - **ID**: observer-skill-protocol-versioning
  - **Tags**: p1, observer-filed, skill-versioning, audit-trail
  - **Touches**: `skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md`, `experiments/observer-protocol-versioning-*.yaml`
  - **Hypothesis**: The observer SKILL.md from PR #493 documents the 5-section protocol (Watch / Restart / Safe-heal / Swift-PR / Log). As Minsky evolves and the protocol changes (e.g. new failure-mode catalogue entries, tighter Safe-heal scope, new rate limits), an observer-filed PR cites the protocol but doesn't say WHICH VERSION of the protocol it followed. Future maintainers reviewing observer-filed PRs from 6 months ago will not know whether the filing matched the protocol-as-of-that-PR. Pre-registration: after this lands, every observer-filed PR cites `protocol_version: v<N>` in its body (the SKILL template adds this); SKILL.md gains a top-of-file `protocol_version: v1` line; the line is bumped via a `## Changelog` section every time the protocol changes substantively.
  - **Details**: (a) Add `protocol_version: v1` to SKILL.md's frontmatter. (b) Add a `## Changelog` section at the bottom of SKILL.md documenting v1's contents. (c) Update the §5 Swift-PR template to require a `Protocol version: v<N>` line in the PR body. (d) Update PR #494's body retroactively to declare `Protocol version: v1` (optional — historical PRs grandfathered, but documenting it is useful).
  - **Files**: `skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md`, `experiments/observer-protocol-versioning-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate).
  - **Verification**: `grep -q "^protocol_version: v" skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md` exits 0; `grep -q "Protocol version: v" skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md` exits 0 (the §5 template carries the marker).
  - **Measurement**: `grep -q 'protocol_version: v' skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md && grep -q 'Protocol version: v' skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md && grep -q '^## Changelog' skill-plugins/observer/minsky/SKILL.md`
  - **Pivot**: if protocol_version churns too rapidly (> 1 bump per month), retire explicit versioning and use git commit SHA of SKILL.md instead (the rev-stable identifier). Decision boundary: > 12 protocol bumps in 12 months.
  - **Acceptance**: SKILL.md carries `protocol_version: v1` + `## Changelog`; observer-filed PR template emits `Protocol version: v1`.
  - **Anchor**: Hyrum, J., *Software Engineering at Google*, O'Reilly, 2020, ISBN 978-1492082798 (versioning protocols + the audit-trail importance — versioned protocols are how Google handles 20-year-old code reviews); rule #7 (vision.md § 7 — chaos engineering visible-not-silent: which version of the protocol filed the failure escalation matters for the post-incident audit); rule #10 (vision.md § 10 — deterministic enforcement; the version field is a deterministic substrate the audit pass can check). Surfaced-by observer plugin design review for slice E.
  - **Risk**: low. Pure additive — adds metadata, doesn't change behaviour.
  - **Surfaced-by**: observer plugin design — the SKILL ships without a version anchor, which is fine for v1 but becomes a debt as the protocol evolves. Anticipatory task filed at v1 ship time.

- [ ] `cross-repo-runner-adopt-tasksmd-parser` — replace in-repo `parseTasksMd` + `pickHostTask` with `@tasks-md/parser` from the canonical tasks.md repo (rule #1 — don't reinvent)
  - **ID**: cross-repo-runner-adopt-tasksmd-parser
  - **Tags**: p1, observer-filed, rule-1, dont-reinvent, cross-repo-runner, parser, tasks.md
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/package.json`, `experiments/cross-repo-runner-adopt-tasksmd-parser-*.yaml`
  - **Hypothesis**: The cross-repo-runner has its own `parseTasksMd` implementation (≈ 230 lines in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts`). The canonical tasks.md spec repo (`~/apps/tooling/tasks.md`, npm package `@tasks-md/parser`) already ships a fully tested parser that handles every metadata format in the spec — including the nested-bullet format that PR #494 had to retrofit into the in-repo parser. Two real-world findings prove the gap: (1) PR #494 (nested-bullet metadata) was a 1-line fix the canonical parser would never have needed; (2) the secondary finding now filed as `parser-accept-verification-acceptance-as-success-aliases` is the SAME class — the in-repo parser is narrower than the spec. Per rule #1, the right answer is to delete the in-repo parser and depend on `@tasks-md/parser` (with a `pickHostTask`-style filter on top, since the parser doesn't know about rule-#9 fields). Pre-registration: after this fix, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts` drops ≥ 150 LOC; the existing 137 cross-repo-runner tests still pass (or are migrated to `@tasks-md/parser`'s own test surface); minsky's own `TASKS.md` is parseable AND yields ≥ 1 eligible task post-aliasing-fix.
  - **Details**: (a) Add `@tasks-md/parser` to `novel/cross-repo-runner/package.json` as a dependency (pinned). (b) Replace `parseTasksMd` body with a thin shim calling `parse()` from `@tasks-md/parser` + adapting the result to the existing `ParsedTask` shape. Keep `pickHostTask` + `isHostTaskEligible` — they're rule-#9-specific filters on top of the parsed result and stay in-repo. (c) Keep the nested-bullet + asterisk-bullet test cases (PR #494 + future) but assert against the new shim's output. (d) Document in `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` § "Accepted tasks.md metadata formats" that the parser is `@tasks-md/parser` and lists what that supports. (e) Rule-#9 substrate in `experiments/cross-repo-runner-adopt-tasksmd-parser-2026-05-12.yaml`.
  - **Verification**: LOC delta in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts` is ≥ -150 lines; `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner` exits 0 with all existing tests passing (or migrated as equivalent assertions); `@tasks-md/parser` appears in `package.json` deps. End-to-end check: `node -e 'import("./novel/cross-repo-runner/dist/task-finder.js").then(m => process.exit(m.parseTasksMd(require("fs").readFileSync("TASKS.md","utf8")).length >= 50 ? 0 : 1))'` exits 0 (post-adoption, minsky's own TASKS.md still parses correctly).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e ".numPassedTests >= 137 and .numFailedTests == 0" && jq -e '.dependencies."@tasks-md/parser"' novel/cross-repo-runner/package.json && test "$(wc -l < novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts)" -lt 80`
  - **Pivot**: if `@tasks-md/parser`'s output shape differs from the cross-repo-runner's `ParsedTask` so significantly that the adapter shim is itself larger than the original `parseTasksMd`, retire the adoption and instead UPSTREAM the missing functionality to `@tasks-md/parser` (file the gap as a PR there). Decision boundary: adapter shim > 50 lines.
  - **Acceptance**: in-repo `parseTasksMd` body drops ≥ 150 LOC; `@tasks-md/parser` is the source of truth for tasks.md parsing; rule-#9-specific filtering (Hypothesis/Success/Pivot/Measurement/Anchor presence checks) stays in `pickHostTask` + `isHostTaskEligible`; existing tests pass.
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (vision.md § 1 — don't reinvent the wheel; `@tasks-md/parser` is the canonical parser for the canonical tasks.md spec); rule #2 (vision.md § 2 — every external dep behind an interface; `@tasks-md/parser` is the interface, the shim is the adapter); rule #3 (test-first — every migrated test case stays); Hyrum, J., Wright, T., *Software Engineering at Google*, O'Reilly, 2020, ISBN 978-1492082798 (canonical-source-of-truth pattern — the spec author's reference implementation is the load-bearing dependency, not a re-implementation). Surfaced-by observer dogfood 2026-05-12 (PR #494 + secondary finding) — both fixes would be free if the canonical parser were in use.
  - **Risk**: medium. Migration touches a hot code path. Mitigation: keep the existing test set as the green substrate during migration; pivot if the shim grows past 50 lines.
  - **Surfaced-by**: PR #494 (nested-bullet parser fix) + secondary finding filed as `parser-accept-verification-acceptance-as-success-aliases` (P1) — both are class-equivalent bugs that the canonical parser doesn't have.

<!-- 9-hour monitoring window 2026-05-06 22:00 → 2026-05-07 ~07:30 surfaced these P1 ergonomics findings — operator-flagged but not loop-breaking. -->

<!-- task-aware-model-router (P1) — operator directive 2026-05-07 surfaced by an external "10-day routing experiment" post the operator shared: a developer logged 150 randomly-sampled coding tasks across 10 days, re-ran each on both cloud-frontier and local Qwen3.6-27B, and found a strong task-class × local-match-rate pattern: file-reads / scanning / "explain code" matched 97 % (35 % of workload), test-writing / boilerplate / single-file-edits matched 88 % (30 %), multi-file debugging dropped to 61 % (20 %), architecture / 5+ file refactors at 29 % (15 %). The operator's translation: "we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time". This task formalises Minsky's per-iteration model router — composes with the P0 local-LLM-fallback substrate (#358 / #365) but with a different decision surface: the P0 fires on budget-circuit-break (emergency); this P1 fires every iteration (routine routing). -->

- [ ] `task-aware-model-router` — daemon classifies each iteration into a routing bucket (docs / single-file slice / multi-file debug / architecture) and routes to the cheapest model that meets that bucket's quality bar, enabling 25-worker concurrent operation within Claude Max 20 budget
  - **ID**: task-aware-model-router
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, throughput, cost-optimization, model-routing, scale, pick-next-after-358-365
  - **Pick-next**: queued behind P0 local-LLM-fallback substrate (#358 merged + #365 on the way) — the substrate must be in main before this P1's slice 1 can land.
  - **Estimate**: 5d (4 code slices ratchet from a measurement preparation slice).
  - **Hypothesis**: External 10-day routing experiment (operator-shared post 2026-05-07): a developer re-ran 150 randomly-sampled coding tasks across both frontier-cloud and local Qwen3.6-27B-on-3090, finding **65 % of routine coding work runs identically on a model that costs only electricity, another 20 % is close enough to accept the occasional miss, and only 15 % genuinely justifies cloud frontier pricing**. Mapped onto Minsky's iteration kinds: brief refreshes / TASKS.md edits / docs-only PRs / metric snapshots / no-code self-diagnose runs are bucket 1 (route to local always); paired-test slices / single-file pure-function additions are bucket 2 (route to local first, fall back to cloud if CI red ≥2×); I/O-wrapper slices / CI-fix iterations / lint-fix iterations are bucket 3 (route to a cheap cloud tier — Sonnet/Haiku — with local as last-resort fallback under budget pressure); substrate slices touching ≥5 files / constitutional-rule changes / cross-package refactors are bucket 4 (route to Opus-grade cloud only; if unavailable, hold rather than burn budget on a degraded run). Pre-registration: post-router, **(a)** the rolling 7d Claude-token-spend per shipped PR drops by ≥40 % vs the pre-router baseline, **(b)** the rolling 7d PR-merge throughput is unchanged-or-up (no quality regression), **(c)** Minsky can sustain 25 concurrent workers within the Claude Max 20 plan budget envelope without triggering `circuit-break-and-notify` more than once per 24 h.
  - **Details**: (a) **Slice 0 (preparation PR — measurement substrate)**: instrument the daemon to emit `iteration.routing.bucket` (one of `docs`, `single-file`, `multi-file`, `architecture`), `iteration.routing.provider` (one of `claude-opus`, `claude-sonnet`, `claude-haiku`, `local-qwen`), and `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` OTEL span attributes for **every** iteration — even pre-router, every iteration is currently `claude-opus-4-7`. Lands `node scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs --since=$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) --json` that reports per-bucket counts, per-provider counts, total tokens, and per-PR-merge cost. This is the rule-#9 baseline; without it, slice 1+ can't measure their own effect. (b) **Slice 1 — pure classifier**: `classifyIteration({ taskBlock, expectedFiles, fileCount, recentPrFailureCount, briefSize }) → { bucket: "docs" | "single-file" | "multi-file" | "architecture", confidence: number }` in `novel/tick-loop/src/iteration-classifier.ts` + 25+ paired tests. Inputs are derived purely from the task block + the daemon's iteration plan; no network calls. (c) **Slice 2 — pure router**: `routeProvider({ bucket, budgetState, claudeProbeResult, localProbeResult, recentBucketSuccessRate }) → { provider: "claude-opus" | "claude-sonnet" | "claude-haiku" | "local-qwen", reason: string }` in `novel/tick-loop/src/provider-router.ts` + 30+ paired tests. Composes with `decideProvider` from P0 #358's substrate (the budget-paused fallback path is preserved as a strict override — circuit-break still wins). (d) **Slice 3 — wire-in + spawn-strategy adapter**: extend `ProcessSpawnStrategy` to dispatch among 4 invocation shapes (`buildClaudePrintInvocation { model: "opus" | "sonnet" | "haiku" }` + `buildAiderInvocation` for local); wire `classifyIteration` + `routeProvider` into `tick-loop.mjs` boot path. The aider invocation hard-codes `--edit-format diff-fenced` per the format gotcha recorded in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`. (e) **Slice 4 — quality gate + auto-tune**: per-bucket rolling 30-iteration success rate (PR merged within 4h CI-clean) is recorded as `routing.bucket.success_rate`; if a bucket's local-routing success rate drops ≥10 pp below its "ought-to" baseline (97 / 88 / 61 / 29 from the load-bearing post), the router auto-promotes that bucket to the next-cheapest cloud tier for 50 iterations, then re-tests local; the re-test prevents permanent degradation while preserving cost discipline. (f) **Slice 5 — 25-worker scale enablement**: memory-pressure invariant in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (`vm_stat | grep "Pages free" < 100k → fire`); single-shared-mlx-server pool semaphore (max 12 concurrent local invocations) so 25 workers don't thundering-herd the local model; per-worker brief-size budget (cap at 20k tokens to avoid local-model context-overflow on bucket 1+2). (g) **Slice 6 — dashboard column + cost-per-PR rolling chart**.
  - **Files**: `TASKS.md` (this block — slice 0 substrate), `docs/task-aware-model-router.md` (operator-facing routing matrix + bucket definitions + the load-bearing post citation), `scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 0), `novel/tick-loop/src/iteration-classifier.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 1), `novel/tick-loop/src/provider-router.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2), `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (slice 3 — extend dispatcher), `novel/tick-loop/src/aider-invocation.ts` (slice 3 — `--edit-format diff-fenced` hard-coded), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slice 3 — wire-in), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (slice 3 — emit `iteration.routing.{bucket,provider}` + `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` span attrs), `novel/tick-loop/src/router-quality-gate.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 4), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (slice 5 — memory-pressure invariant), `novel/dashboard-web/src/routing-column.ts` (slice 6).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `classifyIteration` (25+ cases including the 4 canonical buckets + edge cases: empty task block, task block with only docs files, task block with `Files:` listing 8 files, brief refresh of an already-shipped task). Paired tests for `routeProvider` (30+ cases: each bucket × each budget state × each probe state × each bucket-success-rate band). Integration test: replay 50 historical iterations from `.minsky/workers/*.log`, assert the router's bucket assignment matches a hand-coded expected-bucket label (≥90 % agreement with operator labelling). Chaos test: at 25 concurrent workers, assert no worker waits >60 s on a local-LLM-server lock; assert no `vm_stat` page-free reading drops below 50 k for >2 min.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs --since=$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) --json` returns `{"buckets": {"docs": N1, "single-file": N2, "multi-file": N3, "architecture": N4}, "providers": {"claude-opus": M1, "claude-sonnet": M2, "claude-haiku": M3, "local-qwen": M4}, "tokens": {"prompt": Tp, "completion": Tc, "total": Tt}, "cost_per_merged_pr_usd": C, "merged_pr_count": P}`. Acceptance thresholds (rolling 7d, post-slice-3-merge): **(a)** `cost_per_merged_pr_usd` ≤ 0.6 × pre-router baseline (≥40 % cost reduction); **(b)** `merged_pr_count` ≥ pre-router baseline (no throughput regression); **(c)** `circuit-break-and-notify` events from `.minsky/budget-guard.out.log` ≤ 1 per 24 h sustained at 25-worker concurrency. Per-bucket success rate threshold (rolling 30 iterations per bucket): docs ≥ 92 %, single-file ≥ 80 %, multi-file ≥ 55 %, architecture ≥ 25 % (slack of ~5 pp under the load-bearing post's numbers, accounting for Minsky's stricter CI gate stack vs an unstructured benchmark).
  - **Pivot**: if the rolling 7d cost reduction is <20 % (i.e., the router doesn't actually save money), the bucket-classification accuracy is the bottleneck; pivot to a *learned* classifier (small fine-tune on Minsky's own iteration history) rather than a heuristic one. If multi-file or architecture buckets see local-success-rate drop below 40 % / 15 % respectively for 30 consecutive iterations, retire local routing for that bucket entirely — the post's 61 % / 29 % numbers were on a 3090 with Qwen3.6-27B; M1 Max on Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B may not match those for hard buckets. Don't push local into a bucket where it's not pulling its weight; the rule-#9 mandate against vanity activity applies. If the 25-worker target triggers `circuit-break-and-notify` more than 1×/24 h sustained for 7 days, the router's not the bottleneck — the budget envelope is — pivot to "20 workers, accept lower theoretical max" rather than burning Max 20 plan headroom on retries.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `iteration.routing.{bucket,provider}` + `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` span attrs emitted on every iteration (slice 0). (2) `classifyIteration` pure function with 25+ paired tests, ≥90 % agreement with operator labelling on a 50-iteration historical replay (slice 1). (3) `routeProvider` pure function with 30+ paired tests, composes with the P0 `decideProvider` budget-fallback (slice 2). (4) `spawn-strategy.ts` dispatches among 4 invocation shapes, `--edit-format diff-fenced` hard-coded for local (slice 3). (5) Per-bucket auto-tune fires + reverts within 50 iterations (slice 4 — verified via 7d chaos run). (6) 25 concurrent workers sustained for 24 h without triggering `circuit-break-and-notify` more than 1× and without any `vm_stat` page-free reading dropping below 50 k for >2 min (slice 5). (7) Dashboard shows per-bucket counts + per-provider cost-per-PR rolling 24h (slice 6).
  - **Anchor**: operator-shared 10-day routing experiment post 2026-05-07 (load-bearing prior — the 97 / 88 / 61 / 29 bucket-quality numbers); operator directive 2026-05-07 — "we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time"; rule #1 (don't reinvent — the post's bucket model is industry-validated; adopt it rather than designing a novel taxonomy); rule #6 (stay alive — running 25 workers all the time means more total throughput even with per-iteration quality dispersion); rule #9 (this task's measurement is the rolling 7d `cost_per_merged_pr_usd` query, pre-registered above; success threshold ≤ 0.6 × baseline; pivot threshold <20 % reduction); rule #13 (security-privacy — local routing keeps more code on-device, reducing data-egress surface, which is a positive externality of cost-discipline routing); Forsgren et al. 2018 (DORA's deployment frequency — the router is judged by sustained throughput, not per-iteration latency); Saltzer & Schroeder 1975 (fail-safe defaults — when in doubt about a bucket, default to the more-capable cloud tier rather than the cheaper local one — quality bar holds); the load-bearing post itself: "we're just too lazy to measure it" — slice 0's measurement substrate is the explicit refusal to skip that measurement.
  - **Risk**: medium-high. (a) **Mis-classification — high impact**: a complex task routed to local burns iterations on an under-capable model. Mitigation: slice 1's confidence score; iterations below `confidence < 0.7` always route to claude-sonnet rather than local; slice 4's auto-tune catches sustained mis-routes within 30 iterations. (b) **Local model overload at 25 workers**: 25 concurrent aider clients hammering one mlx-lm.server instance creates queue depth and tail latency. Mitigation: slice 5's 12-concurrent semaphore — extra workers queue rather than spawn additional aider processes. (c) **Memory pressure on M1 Max 32GB**: 25 worktrees × ~500 MB Python aider + 17.2 GB local model + ~5 GB cloud-claude processes ≈ 27 GB resident; tight on 32 GB unified memory. Mitigation: slice 5's `vm_stat` invariant; if page-free drops below 50 k, the supervisor pauses worker spawning. (d) **Quality regression masked by routing**: a router that routes everything-hard to claude makes the local-success metric look good while shipping nothing local. Mitigation: slice 4's per-bucket-success-rate gate watches the actual local-routed rate, not the routed-to rate. (e) **Aider format-gotcha drift**: if a future Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B-Instruct point-release breaks the `diff-fenced` integration, all bucket 1+2 work fails silently. Mitigation: the existing smoke test (Run B in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`) becomes a CI gate (`pnpm smoke:local-llm`) that runs nightly and fires a P0 task if it fails.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-07 operator directive — *"I think as P1 we should optimize minsky token usage so that it always uses various models including local one based on tasks. Ideally we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time"* — citing a foodtruck-bench-post-style 10-day routing experiment where a developer logged 150 random coding tasks across local + cloud models and found 65 % of routine work runs identically on a local model that "costs only electricity". The post's load-bearing claim: *"we're just too lazy to measure it"* — slice 0's measurement substrate is Minsky's explicit refusal to skip that measurement.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — this block provides the 4-bucket classifier + provider router. The parent adds the **role-pin override** (orchestrator iterations always Opus; worker iterations always local-first) so role wins over per-iteration bucket when they conflict.

- [ ] `daemon-local-model-self-tune` — daemon evaluates rolling per-iteration metrics by local-model and auto-swaps the per-machine pin when a better-fitting model is observed; operator approves once, daemon reconciles forever
  - **ID**: daemon-local-model-self-tune
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, local-llm, self-tuning, model-router, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (extends #worker-model-per-machine-config), `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` (new), `.minsky/local-config.json` (rewrite via Strategy seam, never directly edited).
  - **Pick-next**: queued behind P0 #worker-model-per-machine-config (PR #404 filed) and P1 #task-aware-model-router slice 0 — the resolution chain + per-iteration `iteration.routing.{provider,model}` spans are the substrate this consumes.
  - **Estimate**: 3d (1d for the leaderboard fixture + probe; 1d for the recommender + tests; 1d for the auto-rewrite + rollback gate).
  - **Hypothesis**: today the per-machine local model is pinned by the operator at file-edit time (`.minsky/local-config.json`) based on a one-shot recency check (the user's 2026-05-10 swap from Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B → Qwen3.6-27B Dense was a one-time decision keyed off a leaderboard query). Six months later that pin will be wrong: model families ship every quarter; the M1 Max 32GB tier specifically has had Qwen 2.5-Coder-32B → Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B → Qwen3.6-27B-Dense in 12 months. Operator's 2026-05-10 directive: *"minsky should be able to figure out a better local running model for the machine based on metrics. It should be able to change setup."* Pre-registration: post-fix, the daemon reads its own rolling-30d per-iteration spans (per #task-aware-model-router slice 0) bucketed by `iteration.routing.model`, computes a per-model `merged-pr-rate` and `tokens-per-merged-pr`, compares against the periodically-refreshed leaderboard fixture (`scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --json` — pulls SWE-bench Verified + Terminal-Bench 2.0 + RAM tier from the cited sources, capped at the machine's RAM tier), and **(a)** when a candidate model has ≥10 pp higher SWE-bench Verified than the current pin AND fits the machine's RAM AND has ≥3 corroborating sources in the leaderboard fixture, the recommender writes a P0 task block `local-model-swap-candidate-<id>` that proposes the swap; **(b)** if the operator has enabled `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`, the recommender ALSO updates `.minsky/local-config.json` (gitignored, per-machine) and emits a `local-model.auto-swapped` OTEL span with before/after model IDs + rationale; **(c)** rollback gate — if the post-swap rolling-50-iteration `merged-pr-rate` is more than 5 pp below the pre-swap baseline, the recommender auto-reverts the pin and files a Blocked task with the regression details. Without (c), a bad swap could silently degrade throughput for days. Pivot: if leaderboard recency drift is too coarse (the fixture is ≥30d stale most of the time) the recommender is reading dead data; pivot to live-fetch via `WebFetch` against the same sources the operator's recency-check uses, with an offline cache for the daemon's `MINSKY_NETWORK_DENY` mode.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet):
    - **Slice 1 — leaderboard fixture + probe** (1d): `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` ships an offline JSON fixture at `scripts/fixtures/local-model-leaderboard.json` with the canonical sources (`benchlm.ai`, `kilo.ai`, `tokenmix.ai`, `huggingface.co/mlx-community`, `swebench.com`) and per-model rows: `{model_id, ram_q4_gb, swe_bench_verified, terminal_bench_2, hf_mlx_repo, source_urls, recorded_at}`. The fixture is updated quarterly via a manual operator process documented in `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md`; the script's `--refresh` flag uses `WebFetch` against the source URLs (rate-limited, opt-in) when network is available. Pure read-only on read; mutation only via `--refresh`.
    - **Slice 2 — recommender** (1d): `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` exports `recommendLocalModel({ currentModel, machineRamGb, recentSpans, leaderboard }) → { kind: "stay" | "swap-candidate" | "rollback"; toModel?: string; rationale: string; sources: string[] }`. Pure function; tested with 30+ paired cases covering: stay-no-better-model, stay-not-enough-RAM, swap-recommended-with-corroboration, rollback-after-regression, leaderboard-stale-fallback. The "rollback" kind fires only when post-swap rolling spans show ≥5 pp `merged-pr-rate` regression vs the pre-swap baseline (which the recommender persists in `.minsky/state.json` under `local-model-history` on every swap).
    - **Slice 3 — wire-in + auto-rewrite** (1d): `bin/tick-loop.mjs` runs the recommender every N=50 iterations (cheap, pure call). When `kind === "swap-candidate"`, files a P0 task block via the existing `self-diagnose.mjs` writer (composes with #self-diagnose-on-start). When `kind === "swap-candidate"` AND `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1` is set, additionally rewrites `.minsky/local-config.json` via the resolution chain's writer (a new function `setLocalConfigField` in `local-config.ts`; the existing `resolveLocalModel` is read-only). When `kind === "rollback"`, ALWAYS rewrites the config back (rollback bypasses the auto-swap opt-in — the gate exists to prevent regressions, not to require operator approval to undo them). Emits `local-model.auto-swapped` / `local-model.rollback` OTEL spans with before/after IDs.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` + `.test.ts` (new, slice 2), `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (new, slice 1), `scripts/fixtures/local-model-leaderboard.json` (new, slice 1 — quarterly-refreshed), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (slice 3 — adds `setLocalConfigField` writer alongside the existing `resolveLocalModel` reader; composes with #worker-model-per-machine-config), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slice 3 — N=50 iteration recommender call), `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md` (operator-facing — quarterly-refresh process + the `--refresh` flag).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the recommender (30+ cases). Integration test: replay 100 fake spans from a fixture into a fake `local-config.json`, assert the recommender stays/swaps/rollbacks correctly across the bucket boundaries. Live-fire (manual): with `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1` set on this M1 Max, run the daemon for 7 days and observe whether the auto-swap fires for a (then-current) better-fitting model in the same RAM tier.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --recommend --json` returns `{kind, currentModel, toModel, rationale, sources}`. Acceptance threshold (rolling 30d, post-slice-3): **(a)** when the leaderboard fixture's top-fitting candidate has ≥10 pp higher SWE-bench Verified AND ≥3 corroborating sources, the recommender returns `kind: "swap-candidate"` deterministically. **(b)** the auto-rewrite path (when `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`) successfully writes `.minsky/local-config.json` with the new pin AND the next `pnpm minsky` boot resolves to that pin (verified via `resolveLocalModel` integration test). **(c)** the rollback path triggers within 50 iterations of a deliberate regression (operator pins a known-bad model in a chaos run; daemon auto-reverts).
  - **Pivot**: if the leaderboard fixture goes ≥30d stale most of the time (operator forgets quarterly refresh), pivot to live-fetch via `WebFetch` (rate-limited; opt-in via `MINSKY_NETWORK_FETCH_LEADERBOARD=1`) with a 90-day cache. If the recommender's swap-candidate rate is ≥1/month for the same machine (chasing leaderboard noise rather than real upgrades), tighten the corroboration threshold from ≥3 sources to ≥5 OR raise the SWE-bench Verified delta threshold from ≥10 pp to ≥15 pp. If the rollback gate fires more than 1×/month sustained, the recommender's confidence is too low; pause auto-swap entirely and require operator approval per swap.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `recommendLocalModel` ships with 30+ paired tests and the 3-kind decision API. (2) `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --json` returns a recency-checked fixture; `--refresh` updates it from the cited sources via `WebFetch`. (3) `setLocalConfigField` writer composes with the existing `resolveLocalModel` reader; both round-trip through `.minsky/local-config.json` cleanly. (4) Auto-swap is opt-in (`MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`); rollback is automatic. (5) `local-model.auto-swapped` / `local-model.rollback` OTEL spans emitted with before/after model IDs. (6) `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md` documents the quarterly refresh process. (7) Live-fire on this M1 Max for 7 days: the recommender either swaps to a better-fitting model OR returns `kind: "stay"` consistently (no false positives).
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `recommendLocalModel` is the seam between operator-intent and runtime; fed by injected leaderboard + spans); rule #7 (graceful degrade — leaderboard fetch failure falls through to "stay"); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(c) above); rule #13 (security-privacy — auto-swap is opt-in, never silent on first deploy); memory rule `feedback_verify_model_recency_at_filing_time` (this task's leaderboard fixture is the institutional form of that rule); composes with #task-aware-model-router (the per-iteration spans this consumes), #worker-model-per-machine-config (the resolution chain this writes through), #self-diagnose-on-start (the task-block writer this reuses for the swap-candidate filing).
  - **Risk**: medium. (a) **Auto-swap to a worse model**: leaderboard claims don't match this machine's actual workload mix. Mitigation: rollback gate (slice 2 — auto-revert on ≥5 pp `merged-pr-rate` regression); auto-swap is opt-in (operator must set the env var explicitly). (b) **Leaderboard fixture rot**: stale data drives bad swap recommendations. Mitigation: `recorded_at` field on every row; recommender refuses to swap when the top candidate's `recorded_at` is >90d old; quarterly-refresh process documented. (c) **Rapid-swap thrashing**: recommender swaps every 50 iterations chasing noise. Mitigation: minimum 200-iteration "settle window" between swaps; hysteresis on the 10 pp delta threshold (must hold for 100 iterations before a swap fires). (d) **Cross-machine drift**: operator runs minsky on multiple Macs; auto-swap on M1 Max picks model X; on M3 Max picks model Y; debugging "why does this machine ship slower PRs?" gets harder. Mitigation: composes with #worker-model-per-machine-config — the per-machine `.minsky/local-config.json` is the source of truth; auto-swap writes only the local file; cross-machine sync stays out of scope.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) leaderboard refresh cadence — quarterly is the rule-#9 anchor's recommendation; does the operator want monthly? Trade-off: tighter cadence catches better models faster, fixture file churns more. (b) auto-swap opt-in default — should `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP` default to `1` (aggressive) or `0` (conservative — operator approves each swap)? Proposal: default `0` until 30d of stable rollback-gate observations on operator's own machine; then flip to `1`. (c) does the recommender consider model size as a tiebreaker (smaller = faster = better when SWE-bench Verified is within 2 pp)? Proposal: yes — `tokens-per-merged-pr` is the per-machine throughput metric the rolling spans already compute; a smaller model that ships faster is genuinely better at the daemon-throughput goal even at slightly lower benchmark scores.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"What's more, minsky should be able to figure out a better local running model for the machine based on metrics. It should be able to change setup."* The composition with #worker-model-per-machine-config is load-bearing: that task ships the *static* resolution chain (env > config-file > repo-default); this task ships the *dynamic* leaderboard-aware recommender on top. Without #worker-model-per-machine-config's resolution chain, this task can't write its recommendation anywhere persistent.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — the per-machine model auto-tuning is what makes the worker-role default (always local-first) actually correct over time, not just at file-edit-time.

- [ ] `daemon-brief-test-pin-soft-tolerance` — relax `daemon.test.ts` brief-pin assertions to allow legitimate trims while preserving drift protection
  - **ID**: daemon-brief-test-pin-soft-tolerance
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, brief, test-quality
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d

The pins are good drift protection but block legitimate trims. Pre-registration: post-fix, pins use substring-of-section assertions (`expect(brief).toMatch(new RegExp("...intent keyword..."))`) so wording can be tightened while structure is preserved.
  - **Details**: refactor brief tests to assert intent (e.g., "the section names both body-only checkers") rather than exact prose. Identify which pins are load-bearing (test-pinned-string contracts) vs drift-protective (must-mention).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.test.ts`.
  - **Verification**: existing brief-content tests still pass; deliberate prose mutation that drops a load-bearing section still fails.
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, the median brief-trim PR adds 0 test-update commits (currently averages 1).
  - **Pivot**: if soft pins miss real regressions, restore exact pins for the specific contracts that broke.
  - **Anchor**: 9h window 2026-05-07 — multiple workers blocked by pin strictness on otherwise-valid trims.
  - **Risk**: low-medium. Drift could slip through; mitigated by mutation-testing the new assertion shape.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window — workers identified ≥3 pin-blocked optimizations.

  - **ID**: omc-tasksmd-issue
