    ````markdown
    Title: Proposal: optional TASKS.md adapter for /team mode (ecosystem alignment with tasks.md spec)

    ## Summary

    Hi @Yeachan-Heo — proposing an optional adapter so `/team` mode can read its task list from a `TASKS.md` at repo root following the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md), with full backward compatibility (current behaviour is the default).

    The tasks.md spec is a minimal, plain-Markdown task-board format maintained by [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (kanban-style board renderer + linter). Multiple tools are converging on it as a portable task substrate: the upstream `tasksmd` toolchain itself, the Minsky project (constitutional rule: TASKS.md is the actor message store — Hewitt 1973), and any tool that wants its task list to be human-editable and version-controlled in the same file plain-text editors and `gh` already understand.

    OMC's `/team` mode already has a well-shaped persisted task store — this proposal is just to let users point that store at a Markdown file when they want a portable substrate.

    ## Where the integration would land (code-level)

    From a read of `Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode@main`:

    - `src/team/state-paths.ts` — `TeamPaths` declares the canonical layout (`.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`, `config.json`, `events.jsonl`, etc.). An adapter would add an alternate source resolver: when `config.json` carries `tasks_source: "tasks.md"`, the adapter reads `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` instead of the per-task JSON files. Default unchanged.
    - `src/team/types.ts` (lines ~38-58, ~195-213) — `TaskFile` / `TeamTask` shape: `id`, `subject`, `description`, `status`, `owner?`, `blocks[]`, `blocked_by?`, `created_at`, `version?`, `claim?`, etc. Maps cleanly to tasks.md fields:
      - `id` ↔ tasks.md `**ID**`
      - `subject` ↔ task title (the `- [ ]` / `- [x]` line)
      - `description` ↔ tasks.md `**Details**`
      - `status` (`pending | in_progress | completed | blocked`) ↔ `[ ]` / `[x]` checkbox + an extension `**Status**` field for the non-binary states
      - `owner` / `claim.owner` ↔ tasks.md `**Owner**`
      - `blocked_by` / `depends_on` ↔ tasks.md `**Blocked by**`
      - `created_at` ↔ provenance comment
      - `version` (optimistic concurrency) ↔ idempotency key in a hidden HTML comment, preserved on round-trip
    - `src/team/state/tasks.ts:90` — `writeAtomic(taskFilePath, JSON.stringify(updated, null, 2))` is the single canonical write site for `claimTask`. An adapter parallel to this would re-render the relevant tasks.md block (write-back is the harder direction; could ship in a v2).
    - `src/team/task-file-ops.ts:157, 210-243, 321-376` — read/write call sites; the read side is where the adapter reads tasks.md when `tasks_source: "tasks.md"` is set.

    The richer OMC v2 fields (`TeamTaskV2`'s `delegation_compliance`, `claim.token`, `claim.leased_until`) don't have natural tasks.md equivalents; the adapter would lossy-project them on read and preserve them in a hidden comment block on write so round-trips are non-destructive.

    ## Why this is ecosystem alignment, not a single-project request

    Three independent adopters of the tasks.md spec today:

    1. The spec maintainers themselves at [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (board renderer + linter — `npx @tasks-md/lint`).
    2. Minsky (long-running orchestration substrate; uses TASKS.md as its actor message store).
    3. Any tool that wants tasks to be `git`-diffable, plain-Markdown, editable in a plain-text editor without a runtime — a non-trivial superset given how many devs already keep a `TASKS.md` or `TODO.md` by convention.

    For OMC users specifically, this would mean: a team member without OMC installed can still read and edit the task list as plain Markdown; `gh` PR diffs show task changes in a human-readable format; the task list survives independently of `.omc/state/`.

    ## Concrete proposal

    Add an optional `tasks_source` field to `config.json`:

    ```json
    {
      "name": "my-team",
      "tasks_source": "tasks.md"
    }
    ```

    - When unset (default): current behaviour — read/write `.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`.
    - When `"tasks.md"`: read `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` per the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md); fall back to current behaviour if absent or malformed (with a warning).
    - v0 scope: read-only OMC ← TASKS.md (so OMC's optimistic-concurrency `version` field stays authoritative). Write-back can land in a v1 once the round-trip semantics are settled.

    No breaking changes to existing teams; no new required dependencies (a small Markdown parser would suffice, or `@tasks-md/lint`'s parser if you want to share the spec's reference implementation).

    ## Open question

    Does this fit `/team` mode's design intent — i.e., is the canonical task store something `/team` would want to be pluggable — or would you prefer this live as a separate plugin / adapter package (e.g., `@oh-my-claudecode/tasks-md-adapter`) so the core stays minimal? Happy to draft the PR either way; just want to follow your design preference before writing code.

    Thanks for OMC — `/team` mode's blackboard model is exactly the substrate this is trying to align with.
    ````

  - **Last-enriched**: 2026-05-04

- [ ] `devin-worker-auto-exit-after-pr-create` — devin headless worker doesn't exit voluntarily after `gh pr create` succeeds, burning the full spawn timeout on every iteration that completes its brief

  - **ID**: devin-worker-auto-exit-after-pr-create
  - **Tags**: p1, devin-worker, headless, watchdog, observed-in-fleet
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.test.ts`
  - **Hypothesis**: `buildDevinPrintInvocation` (`novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts`, added in PR #572 / 4bb10f9) spawns `devin --print --permission-mode dangerous -- <brief>` and expects devin to exit when the model says "done". Unlike `claude --print`, devin's `--print` mode does NOT exit after the final response — it sits at 0% CPU waiting for an external signal. Observed deterministically across 6 of 9 iterations on the 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run: devin finishes the brief (commits, sometimes pushes, sometimes runs `gh pr create`) then hangs until SIGKILLed by minsky's watchdog at the configured spawn timeout (default 15 min, operator-bumped to 45 min). Iteration record durations cluster at exactly the timeout boundary (`durationMs: 900001` for the 15-min default, `1118428` for a hand-SIGTERMed run). Pre-registration: post-fix, `runLive` polls the spawn's stdoutTail every 30s for an extracted PR URL via the existing `extractPrUrl()` helper (runner.ts:219); on first match it SIGTERMs the child and proceeds to the validated-verdict path. Iteration durations for tasks that DO open a PR drop from `timeout_boundary` (15-45 min) to `actual_work_time + 30s` (typically 8-15 min) — a 2-5× speedup for the autonomous-fleet steady state. The polling interval is the only knob; the watchdog timeout becomes a backstop instead of the common case.
  - **Success**: median iteration duration on the example-service-plugin host drops ≥ 40% (from ~22 min to ≤ 13 min) over a 7-iteration window, AND iteration records emit a new `poll-signaled` marker on the new path.
  - **Details**: (a) New helper in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts` exported as `pollForPrUrl(opts: { spawn, pollIntervalMs, signal }): Promise<{ prUrl, signaled } | null>`. Pure-over-injection: takes the `SpawnLike` result handle and an abort signal. Uses `setInterval(pollIntervalMs)` to read the spawn's streaming `stdoutTail` (need the strategy to expose a `getStdoutTail()` seam — currently only resolved at exit; this is the main API delta). Returns the PR URL + a flag indicating whether the function sent SIGTERM. (b) `runLive` invokes `pollForPrUrl` concurrently with the spawn's exit promise via `Promise.race`. If the poll wins (PR found), SIGTERM the child, wait up to 10s for clean exit, then SIGKILL. Return `verdict: validated` with the polled `pr_url`. The post-mortem scope-leak check still runs (an opened PR with leaked files is still scope-leak). (c) `ProcessSpawnStrategy` (`novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts`) needs a `getStdoutTail(): string` method to expose the in-flight tail. Today the tail is only assembled when the spawn closes; refactor to keep a live `tailBuffer` shared between the data event handler and the new accessor. Bounded to the existing 4 KB cap. (d) Env var `MINSKY_PR_POLL_INTERVAL_MS` (default 30000) plumbed through. (e) Five new paired tests in `runner.test.ts`: poll-finds-pr-then-SIGTERM, poll-times-out-falls-through-to-watchdog, poll-finds-pr-then-spawn-self-exits-cleanly, poll-cancelled-by-abort-signal, spawn-strategy-stdoutTail-accessor.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the new `pollForPrUrl` + `getStdoutTail`. Live integration on the example-service-plugin host: 5 consecutive iterations, target avg `durationMs` ≤ 900000 (15 min) with operator-bumped 45-min timeout still in place (the poll should fire before the timeout). Cross-check against the iteration records in `.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl`.
  - **Measurement**: `cat <hostRoot>/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl | jq -s 'map(select(.pr_url != null) | .notes | capture("(?<ms>\\d+)ms").ms | tonumber) | add / length'` over a 7-iteration window returns < 900000. Baseline today: 1118428–2700000 (15-45 min — the spawn timeout boundary).
  - **Pivot**: if the poll triggers false positives (SIGTERMs devin while it's mid-update of an existing PR description, leaving a half-edited PR body) more than 1 in 20 iterations, tighten the URL extractor to require the URL on a NEWLINE-terminated line (avoid mid-line transient matches) AND require it to appear in stdoutTail for two consecutive 30s polls. If that doesn't fix it, fall back to today's wait-for-watchdog behavior with a clearly-documented "devin headless hangs — bump MINSKY_LIVE_SPAWN_TIMEOUT_MS to 30 min" runbook note instead of the auto-SIGTERM.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `pollForPrUrl` + `getStdoutTail` ship with paired tests; (2) `MINSKY_PR_POLL_INTERVAL_MS` env var plumbed end-to-end; (3) iteration record `notes` field now includes "poll-signaled" when the new path fires; (4) live example-service-plugin run shows median iteration duration drop ≥ 40% vs the 2026-05-16 baseline; (5) one new chaos test under `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/chaos-devin-hang.test.ts` (or equivalent) injects a spawn that emits a PR URL then never exits, asserts the poll path SIGTERMs within `pollIntervalMs + 1s`.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin fleet run — iteration records at `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl` show 4 of 7 substantive iterations exited only on watchdog timeout (durationMs at the boundary). Bridge task on the host side filed as `devin-worker-auto-exit-bridge` in `example-org/example-service-plugin#291` — that's the local supervisor sidecar; THIS task is the upstream fix that obviates the sidecar. Hyrum's Law (every observable behavior of a system will be depended on by somebody) — devin-as-worker is now a depended-on substrate, the auto-exit must be reliable.
  - **Risk**: medium. The change touches the spawn-strategy abstraction (adding the stdoutTail accessor) — must preserve back-compat for `claude --print` callers that don't need polling. Mitigation: poll is opt-in via env var (default off → today's behavior), then flipped on by default once the integration test passes 20/20 over a week.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin autonomous run, supervisor log at `/tmp/minsky-example-service-plugin/supervisor.log` shows the SIGTERM-on-PR pattern operating as a local sidecar.

- [ ] `runner-records-validated-when-pr-opened-despite-nonzero-exit` — `runLive` should treat a non-zero spawn exit as `validated` (not `spawn-failed`) when the spawn's stdoutTail contains an extracted PR URL

  - **ID**: runner-records-validated-when-pr-opened-despite-nonzero-exit
  - **Tags**: p1, runner, verdict, observed-in-fleet
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.test.ts`
  - **Hypothesis**: `runner.ts:152-163` currently returns `verdict: spawn-failed` the moment `result.exitCode !== 0`, throwing away the spawn's stdout/stderr work-product. But in the `devin-worker-auto-exit-after-pr-create` failure mode, the spawn IS opening a PR (recorded in stdoutTail via `gh pr create` output) and then hanging until SIGTERM (exit code 143). The verdict is wrong: a successfully-opened PR is the iteration's success signal regardless of how the spawn exited. Pre-registration: post-fix, when `exitCode !== 0` AND `extractPrUrl(stdoutTail)` returns a non-null URL, record `verdict: validated` with the extracted `pr_url`. Iteration records that today say `verdict: spawn-failed, pr_url: null` for SIGTERMed-after-PR-creation iterations will say `verdict: validated, pr_url: https://github.../pull/N`. Daemon-loop continues to next iteration instead of exiting on `spawn-failed`. Rolling 7d count of iterations marked `spawn-failed` with a salvageable PR URL in stdoutTail drops from ≥1 (today) to 0.
  - **Success**: after a SIGTERM-after-PR-opened iteration, the iteration record reads `verdict: validated` with the extracted `pr_url`; rolling 7d count of iterations marked `spawn-failed` with a salvageable PR URL drops from ≥1 to 0.
  - **Details**: (a) In `runLive` (runner.ts:148), after `inputs.spawn.spawn(...)` resolves, BEFORE the exitCode check: call `const prUrl = extractPrUrl(result.stdoutTail)`. (b) Branch on `(exitCode === 0)` AND `(prUrl !== null)` separately: success path stays `validated` either way; failure path becomes "validated if PR URL extracted, spawn-failed otherwise". Order: if `exitCode !== 0 && prUrl !== null` → `validated` with `pr_url: prUrl`; if `exitCode !== 0 && prUrl === null` → `spawn-failed` (today's behavior). Scope-leak check runs unconditionally for `validated` outcomes (post-merge scope leak is still a scope leak). (c) Iteration record `notes` field gains "signaled-but-pr-opened" marker when the new branch fires, so operators can distinguish "spawn natural-exit clean + PR" from "spawn SIGTERMed but PR was opened first". (d) Three new paired tests: (i) exit-1-with-pr-url-in-stdoutTail → validated; (ii) exit-143-with-pr-url-in-stderrTail (SIGTERM case) → validated; (iii) exit-1-with-no-pr-url-anywhere → spawn-failed (today's behavior preserved). (e) `LiveSpawnOutcome` type's `verdict` discriminator is unchanged; only the decision logic moves.
  - **Verification**: paired tests above. Live integration: re-run the 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin scenario where iteration 2 of `parameterize-auth-posture-probe` opened PR #287 then was SIGTERMed by the supervisor — the iteration record should now read `verdict: validated, pr_url: https://github.example.com/example-org/example-service-plugin/pull/287` instead of `verdict: spawn-failed, pr_url: null`.
  - **Measurement**: `find <hostRoot>/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo -name '*.jsonl' -exec jq -c 'select(.verdict == "spawn-failed" and .pr_url == null and (.notes | contains("signaled")))' {} +` returns 0 lines across a 14-day window (baseline today: ≥4 across the example-service-plugin run alone).
  - **Pivot**: if the new branch triggers false-validated outcomes (devin printed a PR URL in stdout but the URL is a stale reference to an old PR, not the just-created one) more than 1 in 30 iterations, tighten `extractPrUrl` to require the URL appear within the last 4 KB of stdoutTail AND match the iteration's expected `feat/<task-id>` branch slug. If that's still flaky, demote the change to "validated-with-warning" verdict so operators see both signals.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `runLive` returns `verdict: validated` with extracted `pr_url` when `exitCode !== 0 && extractPrUrl(stdoutTail) !== null`; (2) iteration record `notes` field includes a "signaled-but-pr-opened" marker when the new path fires; (3) three paired tests pass; (4) live re-run against the 2026-05-16 supervisor log replays produces the corrected verdicts.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin fleet run — iteration records for `parameterize-auth-posture-probe` (iter 2), `split-api-config-example-vs-app`, `ship-web-platform-eslint-preset` all marked `spawn-failed` despite having opened PRs that were admin-merged. Without this fix, the daemon-loop exits on the first such iteration (per `host-loop.ts:283`), forcing the operator to either restart minsky or run a supervisor sidecar — see `example-org/example-service-plugin#291` `devin-worker-auto-exit-bridge`. Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — the boundary here is "no PR was created", not "the spawn process exit code"). Beyer et al., *SRE*, 2016, Ch. 6 (every signal must be classified — silent spawn-failed eats the PR-opened signal). Companion task `devin-worker-auto-exit-after-pr-create` (above) fixes the upstream cause; this task fixes the downstream verdict so even if the upstream fix doesn't ship, the autonomous-fleet steady state is correct.
  - **Risk**: low. The change is narrow — one decision point in `runLive`, three paired tests. Existing `validated`/`spawn-failed` semantics for the no-PR case are preserved. Failure mode is the false-validated case in the Pivot threshold, mitigated by the tightened extractor.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run, iteration records at `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/parameterize-auth-posture-probe.jsonl` (verdict=spawn-failed but PR #287 was opened+merged), `split-api-config-example-vs-app.jsonl` (similar), `ship-web-platform-eslint-preset.jsonl` (similar).

- [ ] `brief-mandates-task-block-removal-on-shipped-work` — sharpen the spawn brief so devin REMOVES the task block (per tasks.md spec) instead of annotating it with `[x]` ticks

  - **ID**: brief-mandates-task-block-removal-on-shipped-work
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, spawn-plan, brief, p1, rework-prevention, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: The tasks.md spec mandates removing a completed task's entire block (history lives in git log). Minsky's spawn brief in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.ts` says "Cut a branch / ship the code / open a PR" but doesn't explicitly say "if work is already shipped, REMOVE the block". Devin instead "respects existing structure" — ticks `[x]` boxes on acceptance items, adds a `**Status**:` line, leaves the `- [ ]` block intact. The picker then re-picks the SAME task on the next iteration. Adding an explicit clause in `renderSystemPromptOverlay` — "If you discover this task's code is ALREADY SHIPPED (PR open or merged), your ONLY change in this iteration is to REMOVE the entire `- [ ] …` block from TASKS.md. Do NOT add `[x]` annotations. Do NOT add a `**Status**:` line." — closes the loophole.
  - **Success**: After updating the brief, sample 10 successive iterations on tasks where devin discovers shipped work. ≥ 9/10 produce a single-file `git diff` that DELETES the task block (not adds annotations). `grep -c '\\[x\\]' TASKS.md` stays flat or decreases across the 10 iterations (never grows). New regression test in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.test.ts` asserts the brief text contains the literal "REMOVE the entire" instruction.
  - **Pivot**: If devin can't reliably distinguish "work shipped" from "work in progress" (e.g., the PR is open but CI is red, or the merge is half-rebased), fall back to a dedicated `--remove-task <id>` CLI flag the operator runs manually to close out validated tasks — cedes the auto-cleanup to a human gate but eliminates the rework loop. Less elegant but more predictable.
  - **Measurement**: After the brief update, count `git log feat/* --oneline | grep -c "remove.*task block\|closes "` over a 24h window. Target ≥ 1/iteration where shipped-work was discovered. Conversely, `grep -c '\\[x\\]' TASKS.md` should not grow on shipped-work iterations.
  - **Anchor**: tasks.md spec at <https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md/blob/main/spec.md> §"Removing tasks" — "Completed tasks are removed entirely. History lives in git log per the tasks.md spec." (Already referenced in the host's CLAUDE.md / global rules; the brief should reinforce.)
  - **Why**: Observed cost on example-service-api host 2026-05-16: 9 iter records across 2 tasks (`add-releases-cache-findall`: 4 records on already-shipped PR #603; `lma-middleware-canonical`: 5 records on already-shipped PR #614) that should have been 1 record each. ~30-60 min of devin compute wasted on rework.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.ts` (the `renderSystemPromptOverlay` function, around line 93-110), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.test.ts` (assert the new clause).

- [ ] `host-loop-spawn-failed-retry-budget` — wrap spawn-failed verdict in a configurable retry budget so a single bad iteration doesn't halt 8h+ autonomous runs

  - **ID**: host-loop-spawn-failed-retry-budget
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, host-loop, robustness, p1, observability, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring (observed in example-service-api host)
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: `runOneIteration` in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts:283` exits on the FIRST `spawn-failed` verdict. For autonomous orchestration (8h+ windows, 10-20 iterations), this means ONE worker SIGTERM / timeout / crash halts the entire loop. Adding `MINSKY_SPAWN_FAILED_BUDGET=3` env (or similar) — tolerate N consecutive spawn-failures on DISTINCT tasks before exiting — keeps the loop alive through transient failures while still surrendering when something is systematically broken. The retry budget belongs INSIDE minsky (single source of truth for the supervision policy); the external watchdog at `/tmp/minsky-example-service-api-devin/watchdog.sh` is a duct-tape workaround that adds a second moving part.
  - **Success**: After landing the change, a synthetic chaos test in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts` that returns `spawn-failed` 2 times in a row from a mock spawn strategy shows the loop continues to iteration #3 (today: exits at #2). Existing iteration-store tests still green; `pnpm test` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: If the retry budget masks real systematic failures and the operator loses visibility into "minsky has been failing for an hour, intervene" — keep the budget but emit a `WARN: spawn-failed budget consumed N/N — investigate` log line that surfaces in the operator's dashboard. If the WARN is still missed in practice (e.g., logs scroll past, no alert fires), drop the budget entirely and restore single-shot exit.
  - **Measurement**: `cd /Users/fivanishche/apps/tooling/minsky && pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts --reporter=verbose 2>&1 | grep -iE "spawn-failed.*budget|retry.*budget" | wc -l` ≥ 2 (the new tests).
  - **Anchor**: Armstrong, *Programming Erlang*, 2nd ed. (2013), Ch. 11 §"Supervisor Trees" — let-it-crash is bounded by SUPERVISOR retry budgets, not single-shot exit. Current minsky design conflates "the iteration crashed" with "the supervisor should crash". OTP convention: `MaxR=3, MaxT=5` (3 restarts in 5 sec).
  - **Why**: Observed on example-service-api host 2026-05-16 20:00-22:30Z: 12+ watchdog respawns in 2h 30min, every iteration's `spawn-failed` killed minsky. Iter records: `lma-middleware-canonical-header-overhaul` (5 records: 2 scope-leaks + 1 spawn-failed + 1 timeout), `example-model-use-merge-for-partial-updates` (4 records: completed), etc. Each death-and-respawn loses ~30 sec to watchdog poll cadence + minsky startup.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (the early-exit site), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts` (chaos tests for the budget), `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (CLI flag + env wiring), `docs/host-loop-retry-budget.md` (new — operator-facing doc).

- [ ] `spawn-strategy-pre-sigkill-stash` — auto-stash worker WIP before the SIGKILL watchdog fires so devin's uncommitted implementation isn't lost on timeout

  - **ID**: spawn-strategy-pre-sigkill-stash
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, tick-loop, spawn-strategy, data-loss, p1, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: When `MINSKY_LIVE_SPAWN_TIMEOUT_MS` (default 15 min) fires in `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (line ~306), the spawn-strategy SIGKILLs the worker. If devin has implemented but not yet committed (happened on `unblocked-by-task-field-and-lint-2026-05-16` at 21:13Z — 1734 lines of working lint scripts + tests sitting uncommitted in the host repo's working tree), the SIGKILL drops the work. The next iteration redoes everything from scratch. Adding a pre-SIGKILL hook that runs `git stash push -m "auto-stash from minsky timeout <task-id> <UTC>"` in the spawn's `cwd` BEFORE SIGKILL — and waits ≤2s for it to complete (skipping if it stalls) — preserves the WIP for recovery via `git stash list` / `git stash apply`.
  - **Success**: After landing the pre-kill hook in `ProcessSpawnStrategy.spawn`, a synthetic test that spawns a worker which writes 5 files then sleeps past the timeout: timeout fires, pre-kill stash runs, SIGKILL sent. Verify `git -C <fixture-cwd> stash list` shows the labeled stash AND `git stash show -p stash@{0}` contains all 5 modified files. `pnpm test` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: If `git stash` races with the SIGKILL (worker mid-write on a file when kill fires → stash captures half-written content) — drop the auto-stash and instead bump the default timeout to 25 min via `MINSKY_LIVE_SPAWN_TIMEOUT_MS=1500000`, accepting some loss but giving devin headroom. If even 25 min is insufficient, expose a `MINSKY_TIMEOUT_GRACE_MS` env (default 60s) that sends SIGTERM first, waits for graceful commit-and-exit, then SIGKILL.
  - **Measurement**: `cd /Users/fivanishche/apps/tooling/minsky && pnpm exec vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.test.ts --reporter=verbose 2>&1 | grep -iE "auto-stash|timeout-stash|pre-sigkill" | wc -l` ≥ 3 (the new test cases).
  - **Anchor**: Stevens, *Advanced Programming in the UNIX Environment*, 2nd ed., Ch. 10 §"Signal Handlers" — graceful shutdown via SIGTERM-then-grace-then-SIGKILL is the canonical pattern; minsky currently goes straight to SIGKILL on timeout, skipping the grace period that lets the child save work.
  - **Why**: Observed on example-service-api host 2026-05-16 21:13Z: devin shipped a complete implementation (2 lint scripts at 13573 + 11108 bytes + 2 paired test files + AGENTS.md doc + package.json wiring) but timed out before `git commit`. I manually rescued the WIP to a feat branch (commit `824e08b` on `feat/unblocked-by-task-field-and-lint-2026-05-16`, pushed to remote). Future autonomous runs without a manual operator will lose 1500+ LOC per timed-out iteration.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (the SIGKILL site, line ~306), `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.test.ts` (paired tests).

## P2

<!-- 9-hour monitoring window 2026-05-06 22:00 → 2026-05-07 ~07:30 surfaced these P2 ergonomics findings — improvements but not on the critical path. -->

- [ ] `gate-host-load-shed` — shed concurrent host load during a merge-gate vet so vitest stops flaking under 2-3x oversubscription
  - **ID**: gate-host-load-shed
  - **Tags**: gate, reliability, performance, orchestrator
  - **Competitive-goal**: raises minsky's autonomous-merge-rate + lowers change-fail-rate (DORA) on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard by removing the last spurious-skip cause.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 root-caused the residual merge-rate-0 tail: with #590/#592/#593 + the 60-min vet timeout, the orchestrator's scratch vet of the clean MERGEABLE #591 still SKIP'd `gate red: vitest`. Isolated reproduction of the EXACT scratch (origin/main + #591 + `pnpm install` + `vitest`) passed **3039/3040** — the gate failure was a **load flake**: the host runs the orchestrator + worker daemon + other tenants concurrently at load ~14-26 on 10 cores, and a timing-sensitive test flaked under contention. Mitigated in the same PR by `vitest retry: 2` (a flake fails-then-passes; a real bug fails every attempt — Fowler 2011). This companion adds the durable structural fix: during a gate vet, shed competing load — e.g. pause/`SIGSTOP` the worker daemon's active iteration for the vet's duration, or `taskpolicy`/nice the scratch vet onto reserved cores, or serialize gate-vet vs worker-tick so they never run vitest simultaneously. Retry masks the symptom; this removes the cause.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (load-shed hook around `defaultVet`), `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (coordinate with worker daemon), paired tests
  - **Acceptance**: during a gate vet, host load attributable to the worker daemon drops measurably (or vet runs on reserved cores); a 10-run gate-vet sample of a known-green PR yields 0 spurious `vitest` skips (was: intermittent under load).
  - **Hypothesis**: with load shedding, spurious `vitest` gate-red on green PRs → ~0; orchestrator autonomous-merge-rate per productive tick rises (retry alone leaves vet wall-time high under load).
  - **Success**: 10 consecutive gate vets of a seeded green PR all reach `gate green` (no vitest flake); vet p95 wall-time drops vs. the unshed baseline.
  - **Pivot**: if cooperative pause of the worker daemon is too invasive, fall back to retry-only (this PR) + raising `retry` to 3 and accept slower-but-correct vets.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c 'gate red: vitest' .minsky/orchestrate.out.log` over a fixed window before/after → trends to 0 for green PRs; vet p95 from `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` timing.
  - **Anchor**: Fowler 2011 *Eradicating Non-Determinism in Tests*; Nygard 2018 *Release It!* (resource contention / bulkhead); vision.md rule #6.

- [ ] `worker-liveness-detect-by-label-not-argv` — `workerDaemonAlive()` greps `tick-loop.mjs --worker-id=0`; with `--spawn-additional-workers=N` the root argv has no `--worker-id=0`, so liveness detection is fragile/coincidental
  - **ID**: worker-liveness-detect-by-label-not-argv
  - **Tags**: orchestrator, healing, detection, reliability, rule-6
  - **Competitive-goal**: a correct worker-liveness signal prevents spurious daemon kickstarts (avoids interrupting in-flight Opus iterations) → higher effective worker throughput on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 scaled workers to 4 via plist `--spawn-additional-workers=3` (root = worker-0, children `--worker-id=1/2/3`). `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` `workerDaemonAlive()` (line ~53) and the external heartbeat both do `pgrep -f 'tick-loop.mjs --worker-id=0'` — the root proc's argv is now `--spawn-additional-workers=3` (no `--worker-id=0` substring) and no child is `--worker-id=0`, so the intended match is gone. It currently returns true only because a STRAY pre-reload worker proc (old `--worker-id=0 --workers-total=1` argv) happens to still be running; if that stray exits, `workerDaemonAlive()` flips false and the conductor kickstarts the (healthy) 4-worker daemon every tick — disruptive churn that SIGKILLs in-flight Opus iterations. Heartbeat already false-alarms `worker=DOWN`. Fix: detect daemon liveness by launchctl label (`launchctl print gui/$uid/com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run` state=running, runs/last-exit) — the daemon's actual supervisor truth — instead of an argv-substring grep that breaks on any arg-shape change. Update the heartbeat probe identically.
  - **Files**: `scripts/orchestrate.mjs` (`workerDaemonAlive` → launchctl-label probe), heartbeat/monitor script, paired test in a new `scripts/orchestrate.test.mjs` (or extend) with injected probe
  - **Acceptance**: `workerDaemonAlive()` returns true whenever `com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run` is launchd-running regardless of `--worker-id`/`--spawn-additional-workers` arg shape, and false only when the agent is genuinely down; paired test covers both via injected launchctl-state seam; no kickstart when the daemon is up under `--spawn-additional-workers`.
  - **Hypothesis**: spurious worker-daemon kickstarts → 0 (currently latent: would fire every tick if the stray proc exits); in-flight Opus iterations no longer SIGKILLed by false heals.
  - **Success**: with the 4-worker daemon up, `decideHeal` returns "ok" across 5 consecutive ticks even after the stray `--worker-id=0` proc is killed; heartbeat reports worker=up.
  - **Pivot**: if launchctl-label parsing is brittle across macOS versions, fall back to a sentinel file the worker root touches each tick + an mtime-freshness check.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c 'healed.*true\|kickstarted com.minsky.opus-sonnet-run' .minsky/orchestrate.out.log` over a window with the daemon healthy → 0; ledger `healed:false` stays consistent after killing the stray proc.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (supervisor owns restart — detect via the supervisor, not a brittle process-argv heuristic); Nygard 2018 *Release It!* (health checks must reflect real liveness, not a proxy that drifts).

- [ ] `gate-merge-delete-branch-vs-worktree-pin` — `gh pr merge --delete-branch` errors when a daemon worktree pins the PR head branch; the server-side merge succeeds but the gate mis-records it as a failed merge
  - **ID**: gate-merge-delete-branch-vs-worktree-pin
  - **Tags**: gate, merge, worktree, reliability, false-negative
  - **Competitive-goal**: removes a false-negative in the merge path → cleaner autonomous-merge-rate signal + lower MTTR on the `self-metrics-competitive-benchmark` scorecard.
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 gate sweep on #580 logged `#580: merge call failed: Command failed: gh pr merge 580 --squash --admin --delete-branch — failed to delete local branch worktree-daemon-0-minsky-cli-context-aware-ux`. But `gh pr view 580` shows `state=MERGED merged=2026-05-17T02:18:33Z` — the server-side squash merge SUCCEEDED; only the post-merge LOCAL `git branch -d` failed because a parallel worker daemon worktree had that branch checked out (worktree pins the ref). `gh pr merge` does server-merge first, then local cleanup; the cleanup error makes `execFileSync` throw, so `processOnePr` records `merge-failed` for an already-merged PR. Harm: (a) the conductor may re-vet/re-attempt an already-merged PR (wasted bounded sweep slot), (b) the `merged[]` ledger undercounts real merges (corrupts the competitive scorecard's autonomous-merge-rate). Fix: in `defaultMerge`, detect "already merged" (treat as success — re-query `gh pr view --json state` on merge-call failure; MERGED ⇒ success), and/or pass merge without `--delete-branch` when the head branch is held by a worktree (`git worktree list --porcelain` check), leaving branch cleanup to a separate best-effort step (rule #6).
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (`defaultMerge` + `processOnePr` post-merge state re-check), paired test in `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs`
  - **Acceptance**: a PR whose head branch is worktree-pinned still records `merged` (not `merge-failed`) when GitHub reports `state=MERGED`; a genuinely failed merge still records `merge-failed`; paired tests cover both via injected `mergeFn`/state-probe.
  - **Hypothesis**: ledger `merged[]` count matches GitHub's actual merged-PR count over a window (currently undercounts by the worktree-pinned cases); 0 re-attempts of already-merged PRs.
  - **Success**: in a fixture where `mergeFn` throws a delete-branch error but the PR is server-MERGED, `processOnePr` returns `merged`; scorecard autonomous-merge-rate stops undercounting.
  - **Pivot**: if post-merge state re-query is rate-limit-costly, drop `--delete-branch` entirely from the gate merge and reap merged branches in a periodic GC pass.
  - **Measurement**: diff `grep -c '"merged":\[[0-9]' .minsky/orchestrate.jsonl`-derived count vs `gh pr list --state merged --search 'merged:>=<window>'` count → equal after fix.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (cleanup best-effort, never gates the result) + rule #10; the merge is the result, branch deletion is incidental cleanup.

- [ ] `gate-scratch-dir-gc` — sweep-start garbage-collect of stale `minsky-gate-*` scratch dirs, companion to the best-effort teardown
  - **ID**: gate-scratch-dir-gc
  - **Tags**: gate, hygiene, rule-6, reliability
  - **Competitive-goal**: lowers minsky's change-fail-rate / MTTR (DORA) by removing a class of sweep-aborting infra error → improves the autonomous-merge-rate metric on the competitive scorecard (`self-metrics-competitive-benchmark`).
  - **Details**: 2026-05-17 the orchestrator tick logged `sweepError: ENOTEMPTY` from `defaultVet`'s `finally` `rmSync` racing a SIGKILL'd vet's draining children; the throw escaped the finally and aborted the whole sweep (0 merges). Fixed in the same PR by `bestEffortRmScratch` (one retry, then swallow — rule #6, tmpdir is OS-reaped). This companion adds the durable hygiene half: at sweep START, GC any `minsky-gate-*` dir under `tmpdir()` older than the vet timeout AND not owned by a live vet pid, so leaked scratch dirs (from crashes/SIGKILL/operator process-kills) cannot accumulate and cannot cause a future ENOTEMPTY against a half-gone sibling.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (sweep-start GC pass + paired test in `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs`)
  - **Acceptance**: given seeded stale `minsky-gate-XXX` dirs (mtime > timeout, no live owner), a sweep start removes them; a fresh dir owned by a running vet is left untouched; paired unit test proves both.
  - **Hypothesis**: with start-GC + best-effort teardown, `sweepError`-aborted ticks from scratch-dir races drop to ~0; autonomous-merge throughput per 10h run rises.
  - **Success**: zero `ENOTEMPTY`/`sweepError` scratch entries in `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` across a 10h run after deploy (was: ≥1 in the first hour).
  - **Pivot**: if mtime+pid ownership detection is unreliable cross-platform, GC only dirs older than 2× vet-timeout (coarser but safe) and accept slower reclamation.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c ENOTEMPTY .minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` before/after over equal windows → after = 0.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (cleanup best-effort, never gates the loop); Nygard 2018 *Release It!* (housekeeping / resource leak prevention).

<!-- Taskgrind-extraction cluster 2026-05-12: taskgrind (`~/apps/experiments/taskgrind`, 5656 LOC bash + 32 bats suites) is deprecated alongside bosun in favour of minsky. Before it's archived, this sweep extracts the 2 patterns where taskgrind has battle-tested behaviour minsky genuinely lacks. Anti-recs (DO NOT port) documented at /tmp/taskgrind-to-minsky-extraction-analysis.md: `caffeinate -ms` and `taskpolicy -B` (macOS-specific, supervisor's job per launchd `KeepAlive` / `ProcessType`); `lib/watchdog.sh` signal escalation (minsky's launchd/systemd supervisor handles restart per rule #6 — daemon has no internal watchdog by design); `self-copy protection` (TypeScript loaded once at module-instantiation, not byte-offset-lazy like bash); per-repo `slot_lock_file` (already covered by the more sophisticated `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` P0, which uses per-TASK `flock` claims instead of per-REPO locks — see line 426). The 2 P2 tasks below are the residual high-confidence extractions where minsky has a clear gap and taskgrind's pattern is portable to TypeScript. -->

- [ ] `gate-vet-timeout-circuit-breaker` — a PR that vet-times-out should be skipped for a cooldown instead of re-consuming a bounded sweep slot every tick
  - **ID**: gate-vet-timeout-circuit-breaker
  - **Tags**: gate, orchestrator, reliability, candidate-starvation
  - **Details**: Companion to the mergeability pre-resolution fix (this PR makes `defaultSnapshot` resolve TRUE mergeability via `gh pr view` so `pickGateCandidates` actually drops CONFLICTING PRs before the `limit` slice — previously `gh pr list` returned `UNKNOWN`, conflicts slipped to the 25-min scratch vet, and with `limit=2` the conductor perpetually re-vetted #577/#580 and never reached a mergeable PR: the merge-rate-0 starvation). Conflicts are now cheap-skipped, but a PR that genuinely vet-*times-out* (e.g. #580, a slow/hung test) still burns one full `MINSKY_GATE_VET_TIMEOUT_MS` (~25 min) slot on EVERY tick forever. Add a circuit-breaker: record per-PR-head timeout strikes (e.g. `.minsky/gate-timeout-strikes.json`, keyed by PR number + head SHA so a new push clears it) and skip a PR with ≥N recent strikes for a cooldown window, so one pathological PR cannot indefinitely consume the bounded sweep.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` (strike record in `vetErrorToResult`/`processOnePr`, skip in `prepareSweep`), `scripts/local-gate-merge.test.mjs` (paired: strike accrues on timeout; skipped within cooldown; cleared on new head SHA)
  - **Acceptance**: a PR that timed out ≥2 ticks is pre-skipped (logged `timeout-circuit-open`) and consumes 0 vet slots until cooldown elapses OR its head SHA changes; non-timeout skips never accrue strikes; paired tests cover accrue/skip/clear.
  - **Hypothesis**: with conflicts cheap-skipped (this PR) AND timeouts circuit-broken (this task), a bounded `limit=2` sweep reaches a mergeable PR within 1 tick instead of never; orchestrator merge-rate per productive tick goes 0 → ≥1.
  - **Success**: in a sweep where candidates are [conflict, timeout-striked, green], only the green PR is vetted and it merges.
  - **Pivot**: if head-SHA-keyed strike state proves fragile across force-pushes, fall back to a simple per-PR-number N-strikes-then-cooldown with a short TTL.
  - **Measurement**: `.minsky/orchestrate.jsonl` — first `merged:[…]` non-empty tick after deploy; vet-slots-spent-on-timeouts per tick before/after.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #6 (bounded, supervised) + rule #10; Nygard 2018 *Release It!* — Circuit Breaker stability pattern.
- [ ] `gate-scratch-resolvable-ratchet` — add a deterministic check that the local-merge-gate's scratch clone yields a module-resolvable workspace, so the zero-merge regression cannot recur silently
  - **ID**: gate-scratch-resolvable-ratchet
  - **Tags**: gate, ratchet, rule-10, regression-guard
  - **Details**: On 2026-05-16 the Opus orchestrator merged 0 PRs across every tick. Root cause: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs` `prepareScratchClone` symlinked only the *root* `node_modules`, but pnpm scatters a per-package `node_modules` symlink-farm across the workspace. A `git clone` scratch therefore had no nested `node_modules`, so `tsc -b` and `vitest` failed `Cannot find module` / `Failed to load url` for EVERY PR → the conductor correctly-but-uselessly skipped all of them. Fixed in the same PR by replacing the root-only symlink with an isolated `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile --prefer-offline --ignore-scripts` (warm store ⇒ ~3.6s). The bug was silent because an infra-broken vet was misattributed as a per-PR gate-red. This task adds the *rule* so the class cannot return: a check that fails CI if the gate's scratch-prep cannot resolve a known workspace import.
  - **Files**: `scripts/local-gate-merge.mjs`, `scripts/` (new `check-gate-scratch-resolvable` + paired test), `package.json` (wire into the verify gate)
  - **Acceptance**: a deterministic check (a) builds a throwaway scratch via the real `prepareScratchClone` path, (b) asserts resolution succeeds for a representative workspace pkg (`@minsky/adapter-types`) AND a registry dep (`@opentelemetry/api`), (c) fails loudly if either is unresolvable; wired into `npm run verify`; paired unit test proves it goes red when the install step is stubbed out.
  - **Hypothesis**: with the ratchet present, a future edit that reverts `prepareScratchClone` to symlink-only (or otherwise breaks scratch resolution) fails the verify gate before it can merge, so the recurrence mode changes from "silent until a human notices 0 merges" to "caught at PR time".
  - **Success**: stubbing the install step makes the check exit non-zero; the unmodified path exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if standing up a full scratch in the check is too slow for `verify` (>30s), assert the invariant structurally instead — grep that `prepareScratchClone` performs a real install and not a bare root-only symlink — accepting the weaker guarantee.
  - **Measurement**: `npm run verify` exit code with vs. without the install step stubbed; CI duration delta < 30s.
  - **Anchor**: vision.md rule #10 (deterministic enforcement / ratchet); global rule "every bug becomes a rule — prevent the category, not the instance".
- [ ] `daemon-network-resilience-detector` — minsky daemon detects network loss, pauses the iteration timer, and extends the deadline on recovery so long-running daemons survive Wi-Fi drops without wasting iterations
  - **ID**: daemon-network-resilience-detector
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, supervisor, stability, network, taskgrind-extraction
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire into iteration loop), `experiments/network-resilience-detector-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate)
  - **Hypothesis**: today the minsky daemon has only *passive* network-error handling — `claude-health-probe.ts` classifies "ECONNREFUSED" / "transient ENETUNREACH" as `error` rather than `exhausted` and the next iteration retries the same broken path. There's no ACTIVE network-loss detection that pauses the iteration timer or extends a deadline. On a 1-hour Wi-Fi drop, the daemon burns iterations spawning claude (which fails fast), the watchdog fires, the iteration loop keeps grinding — wasting tokens AND consuming the budget envelope that should be defended across the outage. Taskgrind's `bin/taskgrind:1167-1209` ships `_check_network_once` + `check_network` retry wrapper (3 retries × 2s delay before declaring down; configurable via `TG_NET_RETRIES` / `TG_NET_RETRY_DELAY`); paired with `bin/taskgrind:4566-4595` `wait_for_network` loop that pauses the deadline and extends it by the wait duration on recovery. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `NetworkResilienceDetector` ships behind an interface (`isNetworkUp(): Promise<boolean>`, `waitForNetwork(maxWaitMs): Promise<{ recovered, waitedMs }>`) at `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.ts`; **(b)** the daemon's main loop calls `isNetworkUp` after every iteration that ended with `error`-classified output AND the iteration wall-clock was < 30s (fast-failure signal — a healthy iteration with no work-to-do takes longer); **(c)** on detected loss, the loop calls `waitForNetwork(maxWaitMs = MINSKY_NET_MAX_WAIT_MS || 3600_000)` which polls every 30s (configurable via `MINSKY_NET_POLL_MS`); **(d)** on recovery, the iteration deadline is extended by the wait duration (rather than the iteration counter incrementing); **(e)** a new `tick-loop.network.outage` span attribute records each detected outage with `{ start_ts, end_ts, recovered: bool, waited_ms }`; **(f)** simulated 1-hour outage test: iteration count stays unchanged, deadline shifts by ≥3600s, `network.outage` span emitted with `recovered=true`. If (f) over-fires on transient DNS hiccups (≥2 false-positive outages per 24h sustained), tighten the retry logic — require 3 consecutive fail bursts (not just 3 retries in one check) before declaring down. If (f) doesn't fire at all in 30d (no real outages observed in operator's environment), the value isn't iteration-budget-defence (the operator's network is fine) — retire the deadline-extension and keep only the body-text `error`-classification path that already exists.
  - **Details**: (a) New file `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.ts` — pure `decideNetworkState(opts): { up: boolean; reason: string }` (consumes injected fetch seam + retry config) + I/O-edge `runNetworkCheck(opts): Promise<NetworkCheckResult>` (wraps `fetch` with timeout). The check URL is `https://connectivitycheck.gstatic.com/generate_204` by default (matches taskgrind's pattern + zero-byte response = minimal bandwidth); operator override via `MINSKY_NET_CHECK_URL`. (b) `runNetworkCheck` uses the existing `fetch` global (Node 20 native); 5s timeout per attempt; 3 retries × 2s delay (same as taskgrind's defaults). (c) New file `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience-loop.ts` — wraps the existing iteration loop with `waitForNetwork` calls; pure logic (deadline extension) + I/O-edge (sleep). (d) Daemon integration in `daemon.ts`: after each iteration, if `iteration.verdict === 'error'` AND iteration `wall_ms < 30_000`, call `decideNetworkState`; on down, enter the wait loop; on recovery, log the extension and continue. (e) Configurable thresholds via env: `MINSKY_NET_CHECK_URL`, `MINSKY_NET_MAX_WAIT_MS` (default `3600000`), `MINSKY_NET_POLL_MS` (default `30000`), `MINSKY_NET_RETRIES` (default `3`), `MINSKY_NET_RETRY_DELAY_MS` (default `2000`). (f) Telemetry: new `tick-loop.network.outage` span emitted on detected outages, attributes per Hypothesis (e); new `tick-loop.network.up`/`tick-loop.network.down` counters for the dashboard's Watch surface (story 005's 10-metric budget allows this — replace one of the existing slots if at cap).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.ts` (new — pure + I/O-edge split), `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.test.ts` (new — paired tests covering the 5 chaos rows: network-up, network-down-recovers, network-down-times-out, DNS-hiccup-recovers-within-retries, malformed-response), `novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience-loop.ts` (new — deadline-extension logic; pure), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire into iteration lifecycle), `novel/adapters/observability/src/otel.ts` (register new span + counters; if it conflicts with the otel.ts surface limit, accept the increment under threat-model gate), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (document the env vars + behaviour), `experiments/network-resilience-detector-2026-05-12.yaml` (new).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.test.ts` exits 0 with ≥ 7 paired tests passing (5 chaos rows + 2 retry-wrapper rows). Integration test: inject a fake `fetch` that returns 500/ECONNREFUSED for 3 ticks then 204; assert `waitForNetwork` returns `{ recovered: true, waitedMs ≥ 90000 }`. `MINSKY_NET_MAX_WAIT_MS=10000 MINSKY_NET_POLL_MS=1000 node novel/tick-loop/dist/network-resilience.js --self-test` exits 0 after ≤ 12s.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.test.ts --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 7 and .numFailedTests == 0' && grep -cE 'MINSKY_NET_CHECK_URL|MINSKY_NET_MAX_WAIT_MS|MINSKY_NET_POLL_MS' novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience.ts | grep -qE '^[3-9]$|^[1-9][0-9]+$' && grep -q 'tick-loop.network.outage' novel/tick-loop/src/network-resilience-loop.ts`
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis (f). Two falsifiable thresholds: (i) ≥ 2 false-positive outages per 24h sustained 7d → tighten retry logic OR retire deadline-extension; (ii) 0 detected outages in 30d → retire the new path entirely and keep only the existing body-text `error` classification (the network on the operator's machine is stable enough that this substrate doesn't pay for itself).
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `NetworkResilienceDetector` interface + impl ship with paired tests covering the 5 chaos rows; (2) `decideNetworkState` is a pure function (rule #2 — Strategy seam); (3) daemon integration is opt-in via `MINSKY_NET_RESILIENCE=1` env (default OFF until 7d of dogfood validates the false-positive rate); (4) all 5 env vars wired with documented defaults; (5) new OTEL span + counters ship; (6) experiment substrate passes the 3 substrate lints + ci-experiment-runner gate; (7) README documents the env vars + the chaos table.
  - **Anchor**: `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/bin/taskgrind:1167-1212` (the `_check_network_once` + `check_network` retry wrapper); `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/bin/taskgrind:4566-4595` (the `wait_for_network` loop with deadline extension; verified by direct read of the function body); `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/tests/network.bats` (the regression-test pattern this task adopts); Nygard, M., *Release It! Design and Deploy Production-Ready Software*, Pragmatic Bookshelf, 2007, ISBN 978-1680502398, Ch. 4 (Network resilience — circuit breaker probe + half-open recovery is what this substrate IS); Beyer, B., Jones, C., Petoff, J., Murphy, N., *Site Reliability Engineering*, O'Reilly, 2016, ISBN 978-1491929124, Ch. 3 (Error budget — network outages consume the budget; deadline-extension recovers it); rule #1 (don't reinvent — taskgrind's pattern is 3500+ commits of production observation); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `decideNetworkState` is the pure decision, `runNetworkCheck` is the I/O edge); rule #6 (stay alive — the daemon doesn't crash on outage, it waits gracefully); rule #7 (chaos coverage — the 5 chaos rows pin the contract); rule #9 (HDD substrate above).
  - **Risk**: low-medium. Risk is false-positive outages causing unnecessary deadline extensions (a transient DNS hiccup → 30s pause → operator confusion). Mitigation: 3-retry wrapper before declaring down; opt-in via `MINSKY_NET_RESILIENCE=1` so 7d dogfood validates before becoming default; chaos row "malformed-response → graceful-degrade to up (the network IS up, just the check URL is misbehaving)".
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-12 taskgrind-extraction analysis. Verified file:line by directly reading `bin/taskgrind:1167-1212` and `4566-4595` (functions confirmed present, retry-wrapper config confirmed via `DVB_DEFAULT_NET_RETRIES` constant in `lib/constants.sh`).

- [ ] `daemon-stall-detection-per-task` — minsky daemon tracks per-task retry attempts in `.minsky/state.json` and bails out on a task that has been retried too many times, preventing infinite loops on broken tasks
  - **ID**: daemon-stall-detection-per-task
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, supervisor, stability, stall-detection, resume-state, taskgrind-extraction
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` (extend `.minsky/state.json` schema), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire into iteration lifecycle), `experiments/stall-detection-per-task-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate)
  - **Hypothesis**: today minsky's watchdog substrate covers per-iteration timing (`daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` — claude `--print` hang detection), per-PR aging (`daemon-pr-age-watchdog`, `daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog`), and duplicate-PR detection (`daemon-duplicate-work-detection`). NONE of them track per-task retry attempts. A broken task — e.g. one where the worker keeps writing a fix that ships a PR, the PR fails CI, the daemon picks the same task again, writes a similar fix, ships another PR — can ship 5-10 broken PRs against the same task ID before any watchdog notices. Taskgrind's `bin/taskgrind:690,693,3000+` ships `max_zero_ship` (consecutive-zero-ship streak detector — bail at 6) AND a per-task-ID retry counter persisted in `.taskgrind-state` (resume file). Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `.minsky/state.json` schema gains a `task_attempts: { [taskId]: { count: number; lastAttemptAt: epoch; lastVerdict: string } }` map; **(b)** `StallDetector` interface ships at `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.ts` with `recordAttempt(taskId, verdict)` + `getTaskAttempts(taskId): number` + `shouldSkipTask(taskId): { skip: bool; reason: string }`; **(c)** the daemon's `pickTask` consults `shouldSkipTask` before claiming — if the task's attempts exceed `MINSKY_MAX_TASK_ATTEMPTS` (default 3), the task is skipped with a `task-attempts-exhausted` verdict written to TASKS.md as a `**Status**: blocked` field; **(d)** a NEW second axis: `consecutive_zero_ship: number` in `.minsky/state.json` tracks how many iterations in a row produced zero merged PRs (capped at `MINSKY_MAX_ZERO_SHIP`, default 6); **(e)** on a consecutive-zero-ship streak ≥ `MINSKY_SELF_INVESTIGATE_ZERO_SHIP`, default 3, the daemon files a self-diagnose task (`daemon-self-detect-throughput-issues` overlap — composes); on the cap (default 6), the daemon writes a `Blocked: needs-operator-investigation` row to TASKS.md and exits 1; **(f)** the rolling-30d count of "same task ID gets ≥ 4 PR attempts" → 0 (currently rare, but observed during the 2026-05-05 watchdog-window monitoring window). If (f) is already 0 (no real broken tasks observed in 30d), the per-task cap is over-engineered for the symptom — pivot to consecutive-zero-ship-only detection (drop the per-task map) and keep the resume-state foundation for other future state.
  - **Details**: (a) Extend `.minsky/state.json` schema (managed via `claude-exhaustion-state.ts`'s existing read/write helpers — rule #2, single resume-state surface). New fields: `task_attempts: Record<string, { count, lastAttemptAt, lastVerdict }>` and `consecutive_zero_ship: number` and `last_zero_ship_at: number | null`. (b) New pure module `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.ts` with `decideStallVerdict(state, opts): { verdict: 'continue' | 'self-investigate' | 'task-skip' | 'bail'; reason: string; nextState: StallState }`. Pure function — caller injects the current state, gets back the verdict + next state to persist. (c) Daemon integration: after every iteration, read `.minsky/state.json`, call `decideStallVerdict`, write the next state back. `pickTask` queries `getTaskAttempts` and the per-task verdict to filter the queue. (d) When the daemon writes a `task-attempts-exhausted` skip to TASKS.md, it includes a `**Pushback**: task hit MINSKY_MAX_TASK_ATTEMPTS (3); see <PR1>, <PR2>, <PR3>` field so the operator can pick up the trail. (e) Resume across daemon restart: the next daemon process reads `.minsky/state.json` and resumes the per-task counters — no double-counting, no reset. (f) Operator escape hatch: `rm .minsky/state.json::task_attempts` (or `jq 'del(.task_attempts.<id>)' .minsky/state.json | sponge .minsky/state.json`) resets a specific task; documented in `novel/tick-loop/README.md`.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.ts` (new — pure decideStallVerdict), `novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.test.ts` (new — paired tests covering 8 verdict cells: continue × at-cap × self-investigate × bail × task-skip × across-restart × multi-task × operator-override), `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` (extend schema to include task_attempts + consecutive_zero_ship), `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts` (extend tests for the new fields), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire into iteration lifecycle + pickTask), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (document the env vars + the operator escape hatch), `experiments/stall-detection-per-task-2026-05-12.yaml` (new).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.test.ts` exits 0 with ≥ 8 paired tests. Integration test: simulate 3 consecutive failed iterations against task-id-X via injected verdicts; assert `pickTask` skips task-id-X on the 4th iteration AND `**Status**: blocked` + `**Pushback**:` written to TASKS.md. `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts` still passes (extended schema, no regression on existing tests).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.test.ts --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 8 and .numFailedTests == 0' && grep -qE 'task_attempts|consecutive_zero_ship' novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts && grep -qE 'MINSKY_MAX_TASK_ATTEMPTS|MINSKY_MAX_ZERO_SHIP' novel/tick-loop/src/stall-detector.ts`
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis (f). If 30d of dogfood shows zero "broken task with ≥4 attempts" events, retire the per-task cap (keep the consecutive-zero-ship cap — that's still a useful liveness check). If the consecutive-zero-ship cap fires false-positively on a healthy idle daemon (queue empty + no new tasks for hours), raise the threshold to 12 OR add a "queue-emptiness" exemption.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `.minsky/state.json` schema extended with `task_attempts` + `consecutive_zero_ship`; (2) `stall-detector.ts` ships with ≥ 8 paired tests covering the 4 verdict cells × 2 axes; (3) `pickTask` consults the stall detector; (4) on task-attempts-exhausted, TASKS.md gets `**Status**: blocked` + `**Pushback**:` fields; (5) on consecutive-zero-ship cap, daemon writes a self-diagnose task and exits 1; (6) operator escape hatch (`jq -i 'del(.task_attempts.<id>)' .minsky/state.json`) documented; (7) experiment substrate passes the 3 substrate lints + ci-experiment-runner gate.
  - **Anchor**: `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/bin/taskgrind:690,693` (the `max_zero_ship` / `self_investigate_zero_ship_streak` constants — verified present); `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/bin/taskgrind:3000+` (the main-loop zero-ship-count tracking — verified by grep for `zero_ship_count` + `task_attempts`); `~/apps/experiments/taskgrind/docs/resume-state.md` (the resume-file lifecycle — minsky inherits the same lifecycle but in JSON instead of YAML); Lamport, L., "The Implementation of Reliable Distributed Multiprocess Systems", *Computer Networks*, 2 (2), 1978 (fault-stop semantics — the per-task cap is a fail-stop mechanism); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 3 (error-budget — every retry burns budget; the cap bounds the burn); rule #1 (taskgrind's stall detection is battle-tested); rule #2 (`stall-detector.ts` is the pure decision, `claude-exhaustion-state.ts` is the I/O edge — single resume-state surface); rule #6 (stay alive across daemon restart — the resume state is the durable substrate); rule #9 (HDD substrate above — falsifiable per (f)); rule #12 (scope discipline — this is stability work on existing watchdog substrate, not new scope).
  - **Risk**: medium. Risk is a slow-but-healthy task getting marked as stalled after 3 attempts (false positive). Mitigation: the per-task cap is configurable via `MINSKY_MAX_TASK_ATTEMPTS=N`; the `**Pushback**:` field gives the operator full audit trail (which 3 PRs were the failed attempts) before unblocking; the operator escape hatch (`jq -i 'del(.task_attempts.<id>)'`) is one-line. Secondary risk: TASKS.md mutation during the daemon's own iteration (the daemon writes `**Status**: blocked` to a task it just claimed). Mitigation: serialize via the existing `daemon-tasks-md-auto-lint-fix` substrate so the lint failures don't deadlock the pre-PR gate.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-12 taskgrind-extraction analysis. Verified file:line by directly reading `bin/taskgrind:680-700` (the constants block) and grep for `zero_ship_count` + `task_attempts` in `bin/taskgrind` (confirmed present in the main loop). `docs/resume-state.md` confirmed the resume-file lifecycle pattern this task inherits.

  - **ID**: daemon-multi-provider-rate-limit-detector

When the LOCAL stack hits an exhaustion edge (mlx_lm.server OOM, aider rate-limit on a remote OpenRouter-backed config, opencode misroute to a non-existent endpoint), the daemon does not classify it as `exhausted` and retries the same broken path until the watchdog fires.
