- [ ] `cross-repo-runner-per-repo-project-memory` — cross-repo-runner gains a per-host-repo SQLite learnings store so the runner stops repeating the same mistake against the same host across iterations
  - **ID**: cross-repo-runner-per-repo-project-memory
  - **Tags**: p2, cross-repo-runner, learning, bosun-extraction, memory
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/project-memory.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/project-memory.test.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (wire memory into brief assembly), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md`, `experiments/cross-repo-per-repo-memory-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate)
  - **Hypothesis**: cross-repo-runner today is stateless across iterations — when it picks the same task block twice in a row (because the first iteration didn't fully ship), or when it picks two semantically-similar tasks against the same host, it cannot consult what it already learned. Bosun's `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/projectMemory.ts` (1085 LOC) ships a per-repo SQLite store keyed on `{ repoSlug, scope }` with learning entries that carry `{ id, scope, lesson, createdAt, source }`. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `cross-repo-runner` opens `.minsky/project-memory.db` (per-host, gitignored, SQLite via `better-sqlite3` — the same dep bosun uses; rule #1) at the start of every `runLive` invocation; **(b)** when an iteration ships a PR, the runner extracts up to 3 lesson-shaped lines from the PR-body Hypothesis-self-grade `Lesson:` field and writes them to the host's memory keyed by `{ host: <host-slug>, task: <task-id> }`; **(c)** when the runner picks a task next time, `assembleBrief` queries the memory for lessons matching the current task ID (exact match) plus the current host's recent (≤30d) lessons and prepends them to the brief; **(d)** the integration test (`novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/host-memory.test.ts`) seeds a fake `.minsky/project-memory.db` with 2 lessons, runs `assembleBrief`, asserts the rendered brief contains both lesson texts; **(e)** the rolling-7d count of "duplicate PR opened against the same host for the same TASKS.md task-id" → 0 (currently rare, but non-zero; observed during the 4-PR cross-repo-runner v0/v1 ship of cross-repo-runner-v1-live-spawn). If (e) is already 0 today (i.e. duplicate-prevention is not the value), the memory's value is the *quality* improvement on the FIRST iteration of a related task — pivot in that case to a `lesson-utility` rubric where a sample of 5 lessons gets rated by the operator after a month; if ≤ 2/5 are rated "useful", retire the memory and switch to a simpler per-host CLAUDE.md append.
  - **Details**: (a) New file `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/project-memory.ts` exporting `ProjectMemory { open(dbPath: string): Promise<ProjectMemory>; remember(args: { host, task, lesson, source }): Promise<void>; recall(args: { host, task?, sinceMs? }): Promise<ProjectMemoryEntry[]>; close(): Promise<void> }`. Schema: `CREATE TABLE memory (id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY, host TEXT NOT NULL, task TEXT, lesson TEXT NOT NULL, source TEXT NOT NULL, created_at INTEGER NOT NULL); CREATE INDEX idx_memory_host_task ON memory(host, task); CREATE INDEX idx_memory_created ON memory(created_at DESC);`. (b) Lesson extraction — pure helper `extractLessonsFromPrBody(body: string): string[]` greps the `## Hypothesis self-grade` block for the `- **Lesson**:` line; returns at most 3 lessons after splitting on `";"` or `"."` (semicolon-space or period-space) and dropping short fragments (< 20 chars). (c) `host-loop.ts::runLive` opens the memory at start of iteration; after a PR is created, calls `memory.remember({ host, task, lesson, source: 'pr-body' })` for each extracted lesson; before assembling the next brief, calls `memory.recall({ host, task })` and prepends each lesson under a `## Lessons from prior iterations` brief section. (d) The DB lives at `.minsky/project-memory.db` (per-host, gitignored); rule-#13 trust boundary — lessons are operator-readable but not sent to the agent verbatim if they contain a redacted-by-default token (`extractLessonsFromPrBody` runs them through `scrubSecrets` from the existing scan-secrets substrate).
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/project-memory.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/project-memory.test.ts` (new, paired tests), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/lesson-extractor.ts` (new — pure helper), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/lesson-extractor.test.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (wire memory into iteration lifecycle), `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/host-memory.test.ts` (new — full integration), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (document the memory location + schema + privacy contract), `experiments/cross-repo-per-repo-memory-2026-05-12.yaml`.
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner` passes (≥ 4 new paired tests). Integration test seeds a fake DB with 2 lessons, runs `runLive` against a fixture host, asserts the rendered brief contains both lesson texts AND that a third lesson is written back to the DB after the iteration ships. `node -e "const db = require('better-sqlite3')('.minsky/project-memory.db'); console.log(db.prepare('SELECT COUNT(*) AS n FROM memory').get())"` returns `{ n: <n>0 }` after one live `cross-repo-runner --loop` iteration against a host.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 4' && pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/host-memory.test.ts --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 1' && grep -q 'project-memory.db' .gitignore && [ -f .minsky/project-memory.db ] && node -e 'const db=require("better-sqlite3")(".minsky/project-memory.db"); const n=db.prepare("SELECT COUNT(*) AS n FROM memory").get().n; process.exit(n>0?0:1)'`
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis (e). If lessons don't improve iteration quality after 5 operator-rated lessons in 30 days, retire the SQLite store and switch to a simpler per-host `CLAUDE.md` append (the lesson goes into the host's CLAUDE.md, which the next iteration's brief reads via the existing additional-dirs context loader — no DB layer). Decision boundary: ≤ 2/5 operator-rated lessons judged "useful" within 30 days.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `ProjectMemory` adapter ships with paired tests (open/remember/recall/close + schema migration + chaos row "DB corrupt → graceful-degrade to empty recall"); (2) `extractLessonsFromPrBody` ships with paired tests covering the canonical Hypothesis-self-grade block + 3 edge cases (missing block, multi-line lesson, secrets-scrubbed); (3) `host-loop.ts` wires memory into the iteration lifecycle without changing existing tests; (4) integration test ships and passes; (5) `.minsky/project-memory.db` is in `.gitignore`; (6) README documents the schema + privacy contract; (7) experiment substrate passes all 3 substrate lints + ci-experiment-runner gate.
  - **Anchor**: `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/projectMemory.ts:1-1085` (the SQLite-backed per-repo memory; minsky takes the schema + access pattern, not the full bosun shape since bosun's memory is keyed by `{ projectId, scope }` which is bosun-specific); `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/prFeedbackService.ts:32-50` (the `filterSubstantiveComments` + `MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH = 20` pattern for filtering noise from lesson-shaped text); Sutton, R.S. & Barto, A.G., *Reinforcement Learning: An Introduction*, 2nd edition, MIT Press, 2018, ISBN 978-0262039246, Ch. 1 (memory as the value function — lessons are the agent's value-function-of-prior-experience); rule #1 (don't reinvent — bosun's schema and access pattern have a year of production observation); rule #2 (`ProjectMemory` interface + `memory.sqlite.ts` impl); rule #13 (privacy — scrubSecrets gates lesson writes); rule #9 (HDD substrate above).
  - **Risk**: medium. Lesson extraction is the variable part — if `extractLessonsFromPrBody` is too greedy (extracts marketing prose instead of actionable lessons), the brief gets noisier. Mitigation: paired tests cover the canonical shapes; `MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH = 20` filters short fragments; operator can manually expire lessons by editing the DB or deleting `.minsky/project-memory.db` (lossless).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-12 bosun-extraction analysis (`/tmp/bosun-to-minsky-extraction-analysis.md` § Extraction #4 + #12) — bosun has a 1085-LOC `projectMemory.ts` + 116-LOC `prFeedbackService.ts` covering this gap; minsky's cross-repo-runner has no per-host learning today.

- [ ] `daemon-cross-vendor-reviewer-bias-prevention` — CTO-audit reviewer (and any future review-shaped persona) runs against a DIFFERENT model/provider than the worker that produced the output, preventing self-validation bias
  - **ID**: daemon-cross-vendor-reviewer-bias-prevention
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, cto-audit, model-routing, bias, bosun-extraction
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/strategic-model-router.ts`, `experiments/cross-vendor-reviewer-bias-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate)
  - **Hypothesis**: today the `runPostTaskCtoAudit` flow in `novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.ts` runs against whatever model `decideProvider` returns — which, in the budget-paused branch, is the same model (local-Qwen via aider) that produced the original iteration. A reviewer agent that uses the SAME underlying weights as the developer agent will systematically miss the developer's own blind spots (e.g. Qwen consistently writes the same off-by-one bug AND fails to flag it in review). Bosun's `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/modelRouter.ts:148-204` documents this exact concern (the `getBackendTypeForPersona` function returns the configured `alternativeBackendType` for the reviewer persona to prevent self-validation bias — quote from the source: *"For the reviewer persona, returns the configured alternative backend type so it runs through a different LLM than the one used by Developer — preventing self-validation bias."*). Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `runPostTaskCtoAudit` takes a `reviewer-model-override` option that, when set, forces the audit invocation to run against a model NOT used by the iteration being audited; **(b)** `decideProvider` gains an optional `excludeProvider` arg and returns the highest-quality alternative that excludes the named provider; **(c)** the default config sets `cto-audit.reviewer = "claude-opus"` when the iteration ran on `local-qwen`, and `cto-audit.reviewer = "local-qwen"` when the iteration ran on `claude-opus` — bidirectional alternative; **(d)** the integration test injects a fake iteration that ran on `local-qwen`, runs the audit, asserts the audit invocation went through the `claude-print` path (or `MINSKY_AUDIT_PROVIDER` override); **(e)** rolling-30d CTO-audit findings should diverge from worker-output language (cosine similarity ≤ 0.6 on bag-of-tokens) — if the audit and the iteration produce textually-similar output, the reviewer is parroting the worker, not auditing. If (e) doesn't separate (similarity stays > 0.6), the bias-prevention claim is wrong for our specific Opus/Qwen pair — pivot to a different alternative pairing (Opus reviewer with Sonnet worker, or two distinct local models).
  - **Details**: (a) Extend `runPostTaskCtoAudit(opts)` with `opts.reviewerProvider?: ProviderId`; when set, override `decideProvider` for the audit call only. (b) `decideProvider` gets a new optional `excludeProvider?: ProviderId` — when set, returns the *next-best* provider that isn't the excluded one (e.g. if budget-paused excludes claude, return `local-qwen`; if `local-qwen` is excluded and claude is budget-healthy, return `claude-print`). (c) New config block `cto-audit.reviewer-pairing: { worker-provider → reviewer-provider }` in `Config` shape; default `{ "local-qwen": "claude-opus", "claude-opus": "local-qwen", "claude-sonnet": "claude-opus" }`. (d) The fast-path: when `MINSKY_AUDIT_PROVIDER` env var is set, it short-circuits all the pairing logic and forces that provider. (e) Telemetry: add `tick-loop.cto-audit.reviewer-provider` + `tick-loop.cto-audit.worker-provider` span attributes so the cosine-similarity script can read them.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.ts` (extend opts + wire reviewer pairing), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts` (add `excludeProvider` arg + `pickAlternativeProvider` pure helper), `novel/tick-loop/src/strategic-model-router.ts` (config-driven pairing lookup), `novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.test.ts` (new paired tests for pairing logic), `scripts/cto-audit-bias-similarity.mjs` (new — compute cosine similarity over a sample), `docs/cto-audit.md` (document the bias-prevention rationale), `experiments/cross-vendor-reviewer-bias-2026-05-12.yaml`.
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.test.ts` passes (≥ 5 new pairing tests: same-provider-not-allowed, alternative-found, alternative-not-found-fallback-to-default, env-var-override, telemetry-attribute-emitted). `node scripts/cto-audit-bias-similarity.mjs --window=7d` exits 0 and reports `cosine_similarity ≤ 0.6` for the post-fix sample (pre-fix baseline recorded in the experiment substrate for comparison).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/post-task-cto-audit.test.ts --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 5 and .numFailedTests == 0' && grep -qE '(excludeProvider|reviewer-pairing|MINSKY_AUDIT_PROVIDER)' novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts && node scripts/cto-audit-bias-similarity.mjs --window=7d --json | jq -e '.cosine_similarity <= 0.6'`
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis (e). If Opus-reviewer-of-Qwen-worker doesn't separate (cosine > 0.6), Opus and Qwen are too aligned in our specific use case — try Opus reviewer of GPT-5 worker (different vendor + different family). If no vendor pairing separates, the bias-prevention thesis is wrong for code review and we retire the feature.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `runPostTaskCtoAudit` accepts `reviewerProvider` override + reads `MINSKY_AUDIT_PROVIDER` env; (2) `decideProvider` accepts `excludeProvider` and returns alternative or falls back; (3) Config carries `cto-audit.reviewer-pairing` with the default 3 pairings; (4) ≥ 5 new paired tests cover the pairing logic + env override; (5) `cto-audit-bias-similarity.mjs` ships and exits 0 with ≤ 0.6 cosine; (6) `docs/cto-audit.md` documents the rationale + the literature anchor; (7) telemetry attributes ship and are queryable.
  - **Anchor**: `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/modelRouter.ts:118-180` (the cross-vendor pairing logic and the JSDoc rationale verbatim); Sunstein, C.R., *#Republic: Divided Democracy in the Age of Social Media*, Princeton, 2017, ISBN 978-0691175515, Ch. 3 (group polarisation — same-vendor reviewers polarise the same biases as the worker); Surowiecki, J., *The Wisdom of Crowds*, Anchor, 2005, ISBN 978-0385721707, Ch. 2 (diversity-of-opinion as the load-bearing pre-condition for crowd accuracy); rule #1 (don't reinvent — bosun has the concept named and shaped); rule #2 (`pickAlternativeProvider` is a Strategy seam); rule #7 (chaos table — `MINSKY_AUDIT_PROVIDER=invalid-provider` → graceful-degrade to default pairing, not crash); rule #9 (HDD measurement above — cosine similarity is the falsifiable metric).
  - **Risk**: medium. Cosine similarity is a crude metric for "different conclusions" — a sophisticated reviewer could legitimately reach a similar conclusion via different reasoning. Mitigation: operator manually rates a sample of 5 audits post-rollout; if the rating disagrees with the cosine-similarity verdict, replace the metric with a rubric-based audit comparison.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-12 bosun-extraction analysis — verified by reading `modelRouter.ts:148-204` which carries the cross-vendor logic + the explicit JSDoc rationale.

- [ ] `daemon-pr-feedback-extraction` — daemon extracts substantive PR review comments from merged daemon PRs and feeds them into the next iteration's brief, learning from human feedback
  - **ID**: daemon-pr-feedback-extraction
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, learning, pr-feedback, bosun-extraction
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire post-merge extraction), `experiments/pr-feedback-extraction-2026-05-12.yaml` (new — rule-#9 substrate)
  - **Hypothesis**: today the daemon does not consult human review comments on its own merged PRs. When an operator leaves a review comment like "this would be cleaner with a switch statement" on PR #N, the next iteration on a similar task makes the same mistake. Bosun's `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/prFeedbackService.ts` (116 LOC total) ships `filterSubstantiveComments` (filters noise via 8 regex patterns: `^lgtm$`, `^looks good`, `^\+1$`, `:thumbsup:`, `^approved$`, `^nice work`, `^ship it`, `^nit:`) plus `MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH = 20` and `extractLearningsFromComments` (truncates at 300 chars, normalises whitespace, prefixes with `[<path>] PR feedback (<user>):`). Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** after a daemon PR merges, the daemon calls `gh pr view <n> --json reviews,comments,reviewThreads --jq ...` to fetch all review comments; **(b)** `filterSubstantiveComments` drops the 8 noise patterns + comments < 20 chars; **(c)** the remaining substantive lessons go into the next iteration's brief under a `## Lessons from recent reviews on this repo` section (capped at 5 most-recent, 300 chars each); **(d)** the integration test ships 4 review comments (2 noise + 2 substantive), asserts only the substantive 2 reach the brief; **(e)** rolling-30d count of repeated review comments (operator opens a comment that semantically matches one from a prior PR on the same daemon iteration target) drops by ≥ 50 % compared to the 30d pre-fix baseline. If (e) doesn't move (count stays flat), the issue is not that the lessons aren't reaching the brief — it's that the daemon's persona doesn't act on lessons in the brief. Pivot in that case: retire the brief-prepend approach and switch to a stricter pre-PR substrate lint that auto-rejects diffs matching a flagged anti-pattern from prior reviews.
  - **Details**: (a) New file `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.ts` — pure `extractFeedback(reviewBodies: PrReviewComment[]): string[]` using bosun's noise-pattern set + minsky's existing `scrubSecrets` for trust-boundary safety. (b) New file `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-fetcher.ts` — I/O-edge `fetchPrReviewComments(prNumber, gh = realGh): Promise<PrReviewComment[]>` that wraps `gh pr view --json` with a Strategy seam for testing. (c) Wire into `daemon.ts` post-merge — when an iteration detects a `MERGED` state on a daemon-authored PR, fetch + extract + store into the project-memory DB (composes with `cross-repo-runner-per-repo-project-memory` above — same DB, schema-compatible). (d) Brief assembly reads the last ≤ 5 substantive lessons from project-memory and prepends them under `## Lessons from recent reviews on this repo`. (e) The 8 noise regex patterns are copied byte-for-byte from bosun's `prFeedbackService.ts:19-28` (rule #1 — battle-tested set).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.ts` (new — pure helpers; copy bosun's noise patterns), `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.test.ts` (new — paired tests covering 8 noise rows + 4 substantive rows + the truncate-and-prefix shape), `novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-fetcher.ts` (new — I/O edge with `ghFn` seam), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (post-merge hook), `experiments/pr-feedback-extraction-2026-05-12.yaml` (new).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.test.ts` passes (≥ 12 new paired tests). Integration test injects 4 review comments via the `ghFn` seam, asserts only 2 substantive comments reach the rendered brief.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.test.ts --reporter=json 2>/dev/null | jq -e '.numPassedTests >= 12 and .numFailedTests == 0' && grep -cE 'lgtm|looks good|\\\\+1|thumbsup|approved|nice work|ship it|^nit:' novel/tick-loop/src/pr-feedback-extractor.ts | grep -qE '^[8-9]$|^[1-9][0-9]+$'`
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis (e). If lessons don't reduce repeat review comments, retire brief-prepend and switch to an anti-pattern lint (catch the offending pattern at the diff stage, not the prompt stage).
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `extractFeedback` ships with the 8 bosun noise patterns copied verbatim + MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH = 20; (2) paired tests cover every noise pattern + ≥ 4 substantive rows; (3) `fetchPrReviewComments` ships with the `ghFn` injectable seam; (4) daemon's post-merge hook wires extraction into project-memory; (5) brief assembly prepends ≤ 5 recent lessons; (6) experiment substrate passes the 3 substrate lints + ci-experiment-runner gate.
  - **Anchor**: `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/prFeedbackService.ts:19-28` (the 8 noise patterns); `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/prFeedbackService.ts:30` (`MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH = 20`); `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/prFeedbackService.ts:32-49` (filter-and-format pattern); Argyris, C., *Teaching Smart People How to Learn*, Harvard Business Review, May–June 1991 (the gap between espoused theory and theory-in-use — agents espouse "I will learn from feedback" but their iteration loop has no feedback ingress without this substrate); rule #1 (don't reinvent — bosun's noise set is battle-tested); rule #2 (`extractFeedback` is a pure function; `fetchPrReviewComments` is the I/O edge with a `ghFn` seam — both behind a single `PrFeedbackAdapter` interface).
  - **Risk**: low-medium. Risk is in the brief becoming noisy if 5 lessons of 300 chars each gets prepended every iteration. Mitigation: cap at 5 most-recent (last 30d); operator can lower the cap via `MINSKY_PR_FEEDBACK_CAP=2`.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-12 bosun-extraction analysis. Verified file:line by reading `prFeedbackService.ts:1-60` directly (8 noise patterns + MIN_COMMENT_LENGTH constant confirmed).

  - **ID**: dependabot-bumps-dep-regression-triage

  - **Hypothesis**: 9h window 2026-05-07: 8 dependabot PRs (`actions/setup-python` 5→6, `actions/upload-artifact` 4→7, `markdownlint-cli2` 0.15→0.22, `hono` 4.12.16→4.12.18, OTEL 0.57.2→0.217.0 ×3, etc.) all failing CI. Most are major bumps with breaking-change semantics; some are patch bumps that should pass. Pre-registration: post-fix, dependabot PRs split by semver: patch+minor auto-merge if CI green; major bumps file a `dep-upgrade-<package>` task with the breaking-change diff and require operator approval. Rolling-7d failing-dependabot-PR count → ≤2.
  - **Details**: `.github/dependabot.yml` configures `versioning-strategy: increase` for patch + minor; major bumps go to a separate group with `labels: [needs-operator]`. Existing 8 PRs: triage manually — close the major OTEL bumps as out-of-scope, retry the patch bumps after main updates.
  - **Files**: `.github/dependabot.yml`, `docs/dependency-policy.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired test: synthetic patch-bump PR auto-merges; major-bump PR opens with `needs-operator` label.
  - **Measurement**: count of `closed-as-not-planned` dependabot PRs over 30d ≤ 1/month average.
  - **Pivot**: if patch bumps still cause regressions (transitive deps), tighten to lockfile-only updates.
  - **Anchor**: 9h window 2026-05-07; Dependabot best practices.
  - **Risk**: low.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window — 8 stuck dependabot PRs.

- [ ] `spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring` — substrate for safely running N (4-10) parallel workers with a monitor that auto-unblocks stuck children + files incident tasks
  - **ID**: spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, supervisor, parallel, watchdog, follow-up
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Hypothesis**: Operator question 2026-05-07: "should and can we spawn 10 workers, all monitored by this window that unblocks them & files tasks so that next time minsky unblocks itself". The 9h window demonstrated I was that monitor manually — killed the worker-1 hang, closed duplicate PRs, fixed body-fail PRs, rebased stuck PRs. Pre-registration: post-fix, a monitor process spawned by `pnpm minsky --spawn-additional-workers=N --watchdog` performs all 4 of those interventions automatically and emits incident spans + TASKS.md filings for each. Rolling-7d operator-manual-intervention count → 0 across N=4 workers; → ≤1/day across N=10.
  - **Details**: (a) New flag `--watchdog` on the root `pnpm minsky` invocation. (b) Watchdog process (separate from worker daemons): runs every 60s, queries `pgrep --parent <worker-pid>` for stuck children (CPU<5% for >15min) → SIGKILLs them. (c) Queries `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot"` for: PRs CONFLICTING >2h → invokes the rebase watchdog (#daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog); PRs failing only on body-only checks → patches body. (d) For each intervention, files a TASKS.md entry under `## P2` with `**Auto-filed-by**: spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring` so the daemon learns the unblock pattern over time. (e) Composes with `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` (P0), `daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog` (P0), `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion` (P0), `daemon-duplicate-work-detection` (P0) — those four shipped is the precondition for safe N≥4.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/bin/watchdog.mjs` (new bin), `novel/tick-loop/src/watchdog.ts` (pure decisions for kill / rebase / body-patch), `novel/tick-loop/src/watchdog.test.ts` (paired tests for each intervention), `package.json` `bin: { minsky-watchdog: ... }`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each intervention class. Integration test: spawn 2 fake workers, simulate a hang, watchdog kills + files task within 60s.
  - **Measurement**: `count(operator-manual-interventions)` per worker per day → see hypothesis thresholds. Concrete log probe: `grep -c 'minsky: operator manually killed' .minsky/workers/*.log` over 7d → 0 (ideal); 1-3 is acceptable while substrate matures.
  - **Pivot**: if the watchdog itself crashes (silence-is-failure on the watchdog), the operator's manual intervention rate stays high — pivot to `launchd KeepAlive` + a separate `minsky-watchdog` plist so the watchdog has its own respawn.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-07 — "monitor + unblock + file tasks so next time minsky unblocks itself"; `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` parent task; rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure decisions); rule #6 (let-it-crash — watchdog kills hung children); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD).
  - **Risk**: medium. The watchdog has destructive power (SIGKILL, force-push, body-patch). Mitigations: cap-3 retries before escalating to `Blocked: needs-operator`; all interventions logged + incident-task-filed; opt-out via `MINSKY_WATCHDOG_DRY_RUN=1` for first deploy.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-07 directive ("file tasks for all findings and bugs… should we spawn 10 workers"); 9h monitoring window 2026-05-06/07 demonstrated all 4 intervention classes manually.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — this block provides the watchdog substrate (kill stuck child, rebase stuck PR, body-patch). The parent adds the **cross-layer** chaos slice (orchestrator-death-recovery and worker-hang-detection-from-orchestrator-side via `chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` and `chaos-worker-hang.mjs`).

- [ ] `brief-trim-coordinator` — workers compete on the same brief sections; need a coordinator so one PR/iter trims and others abstain
  - **ID**: brief-trim-coordinator
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, optimization, parallel-launch
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: 9h window 2026-05-07 with 2 workers: both shipped brief-trim commits on overlapping sections → multiple rebases needed and ~1/3 of optimization commits got conflicts. With N=10 workers this becomes severe. Pre-registration: post-fix, `acquireTaskClaim`-style lock on `buildDaemonBrief` itself — only the worker holding the brief-trim claim may touch `daemon.ts` brief constants per iteration; others fall back to `optimization: none-this-iteration`.
  - **Details**: extend `acquireTaskClaim` with a per-resource lock (`brief-trim` resource) with TTL 10 min. The optimization-discipline gate in `buildDaemonBrief` reads this and either greenlights or steers to alternative optimization classes (round-trip elimination, log-line dedup) when locked.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-claim.ts` (extend with resource locks), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (brief gate reads the lock).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for resource lock; brief contains coordinator hint when locked.
  - **Measurement**: post-deploy, brief-trim-commit conflicts in 7d → 0 across active workers.
  - **Pivot**: if resource lock causes optimization-gate noops too often, drop the lock and accept the conflict cost.
  - **Anchor**: 9h window 2026-05-07 — observed brief-trim conflicts; `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` parent task.
  - **Risk**: low.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07.

- [ ] First user-story integration test passes (001) — tracker
  - **ID**: first-integration-test
  - **Tags**: testing, validation, tracker
  - **Estimate**: 6h (decomposed across 3 sub-tasks)
  - **Blocked by**: first-integration-test-nightly-self-hosted
  - **Hypothesis**: A 60-minute compressed simulation reproduces the failure modes that matter for an 8h overnight run with ≥80 % coverage of the failure-mode rows declared in the user-story file, while keeping CI runtime under 10 minutes. Per the documented Pivot below (reframe as 10-min smoke + nightly self-hosted), the work is decomposed into three sub-tasks; this entry is the tracker that closes when all three ship.
  - **Details**: Decomposed on 2026-05-04 per the parent task's documented Pivot. Sub-task 1 (`first-integration-test-coverage-manifest`) ships the coverage manifest test. Sub-task 2 (`first-integration-test-mock-tick-loop`) builds a mock daemon for the in-process 10-min smoke. Sub-task 3 (`first-integration-test-nightly-self-hosted`) wires the nightly self-hosted-runner workflow for the 7 OS-level chaos rows. This block remains as the coordination contract — Hypothesis / Success / Pivot / Measurement / Anchor are the parent-level invariants; the sub-tasks each carry their own rule-#9 fields scoped to their slice.
  - **Verification**: `npm test user-stories/001-loop-runs-overnight.test.ts` passes locally and on CI; OTEL collector receives ≥1 span per task type; CI workflow shows green. (Each sub-task's own Verification cell is the load-bearing one; this tracker closes when all three pass.)
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run user-stories/001-coverage-manifest.test.ts` exits 0 (sub-task 1) AND `pnpm vitest run novel/tick-loop` exits 0 (sub-task 2) AND `gh run list --workflow nightly-overnight-sim.yml --status success --limit 1 --json conclusion --jq '.[0].conclusion'` returns `success` (sub-task 3).
  - **Pivot**: if the 60-min sim's CI runtime exceeds 10 min OR misses >2 of the user-story's failure modes → reframe as a pair (10-min smoke in CI + nightly self-hosted run that does the full 60-min). **Pivot fired 2026-05-04** — decomposition into 3 sub-tasks landed; this tracker now coordinates the sub-tasks. If even the sub-task path fails (sub-task 2's smoke can't fit in 10 min OR sub-task 3's self-hosted runner is unreachable), the story's overnight assumption is wrong and the story needs splitting.
  - **Acceptance**: All three sub-tasks closed; coverage manifest's ≥80 % ratio holds; nightly self-hosted run lands at least once `success`.
  - **Anchor**: Basiri et al., "Principles of Chaos Engineering", *IEEE Software* 2016 (steady-state hypothesis); Beck, *Extreme Programming Explained*, 1999 (CI keeps the build fast).
  - **Risk**: 60min compressed sim may miss real overnight failure modes (memory leaks, log rotation, OS sleep). Documented gap; sub-task 3's nightly self-hosted run is the mitigation.

- [ ] Nightly overnight-sim workflow on a self-hosted runner
  - **ID**: first-integration-test-nightly-self-hosted
  - **Parent**: first-integration-test
  - **Tags**: testing, infra, ci, dormant-until-self-hosted-runner
  - **Estimate**: 4h (when self-hosted runner is available)
  - **Hypothesis**: A nightly workflow (`.github/workflows/nightly-overnight-sim.yml`) running the full 60-min sim on a self-hosted runner — using the mock daemon from sub-task 2 — covers the 7 OS-level chaos rows (2, 5, 6, 7, 8, 11, 12) of user-story 001's failure-mode table that GH-hosted runners cannot exercise (libfaketime, iptables, tc qdisc, dd, pmset), without burning CI minutes on the hot per-PR path.
  - **Details**: Triggers when sub-task 2's mock-tick-loop ships AND a self-hosted runner is available (mirrors the precedent of `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` and `lighthouse-self-hosted-runner-pivot`). Workflow uses `runs-on: [self-hosted, linux]`, runs nightly at low-stakes UTC hours, and exercises one randomly-chosen OS-level chaos row per night per `user-stories/001-loop-runs-overnight.md`'s weekly-fault-injection prose. Failures escalate to a Watch-level notification per the user-story's chaos-verification section.
  - **Files**: `.github/workflows/nightly-overnight-sim.yml`, `docs/self-hosted-runner.md` (shared with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if it has fired)
  - **Verification**: at least one nightly run lands `success`; the run touches at least one of rows 2, 5, 6, 7, 8, 11, 12 (the OS-fault rows in the manifest).
  - **Measurement**: `gh run list --workflow nightly-overnight-sim.yml --branch main --status success --limit 5 --json conclusion --jq '[.[] | select(.conclusion=="success")] | length >= 1'` exits 0 with `true`.
  - **Pivot**: if self-hosted-runner maintenance burden exceeds the empirical signal value (e.g., the runner needs >1 manual intervention per quarter) OR if no self-hosted runner becomes available within 90 days of sub-task 2 shipping, retire this dormant task and document the OS-level chaos rows as a permanent declared deviation in `user-stories/001-loop-runs-overnight.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: this task fires only after sub-task 2 ships AND a self-hosted runner is available; otherwise it remains a dormant scout entry per the parent `first-integration-test` task's documented Pivot.
  - **Anchor**: Basiri et al., "Principles of Chaos Engineering", *IEEE Software* 2016 (the documented Pivot from `first-integration-test`'s rule-#9 block — coverage of OS-level rows belongs in a self-hosted runner with real OS primitives); Forsgren, Humble, Kim, *Accelerate*, IT Revolution Press, 2018 (DORA test reliability — a CI gate that doesn't run reliably teaches the team to ignore failure; the nightly cadence is the reliability bound).
  - **Risk**: self-hosted runners introduce supply-chain risk (a compromised runner can leak secrets). Mitigation: scope the runner to public-repo / non-secret jobs only; share infrastructure with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if both fire (cost amortisation); standard GH guidance.

- [ ] `brief-instructs-exit-after-pr-open` — brief should tell devin to exit cleanly (`process.exit(0)`) immediately after `gh pr create` succeeds, instead of running to 15-min timeout

  - **ID**: brief-instructs-exit-after-pr-open
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, spawn-plan, brief, cost, p2, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: The devin worker spawned by `ProcessSpawnStrategy` doesn't reliably exit when its iteration's work is complete (PR opened, tests passed). Observed: `lma-middleware-canonical-header-overhaul` spawn at 16:15Z opened PR #614 at 16:29Z (14 min into the iteration) then ran to the 15-min `MINSKY_LIVE_SPAWN_TIMEOUT_MS` SIGKILL — wasted 1 min of compute. `example-model-use-merge-for-partial-updates` opened PR #616 then continued for ~3 more minutes before SIGKILL — wasted 3 min. Adding a "Exit cleanly with exit code 0 immediately after `gh pr create` succeeds — do NOT wait for CI feedback (the next iteration handles CI-fix loops)" clause to the brief in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.ts` cuts the wall-clock cost of each iteration by ~10-30%.
  - **Success**: After updating the brief, sample 5 successive validated iterations. Wall-clock duration distribution shifts: today's median ≈ 12-15 min; target post-fix median ≤ 8 min (PR-open cadence). Verified by `cat .minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl | jq '.notes' | grep -oE '[0-9]+ms' | sort -n | head -10 | awk '{sum+=$1} END {print sum/NR}'`.
  - **Pivot**: If devin exits before PR CI feedback is available (preventing immediate-react-to-red-CI), restore the previous "wait until something happens" behaviour AND reduce `MINSKY_LIVE_SPAWN_TIMEOUT_MS` default to 8 min — accepting that some long iterations get killed but cheap ones don't waste budget. (Trades worst-case for typical-case.)
  - **Measurement**: After brief update, `for f in .minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl; do tail -1 $f | jq -r '.notes' | grep -oE '[0-9]+ms' | head -1; done | sort -n | awk '{print $1/1000}'` — median should drop from ~720s to ≤ 480s.
  - **Pivot escape hatch**: `MINSKY_BRIEF_WAIT_AFTER_PR_OPEN=true` env reverts to the legacy "run to timeout" behavior in case operators discover CI-fix loops need the wait.
  - **Anchor**: Ousterhout, *A Philosophy of Software Design*, 2nd ed., Ch. 12 §"Pull Complexity Downwards" — the cheap-iteration case shouldn't pay for the worst-case ceiling. Adapt the brief so exit-when-done is explicit; let timeout be the last-resort kill switch, not the typical exit path.
  - **Why**: At ~$1-2/min for headless agent compute (rough), an extra 1-3 min per iteration × 10-20 iterations / 8h = 10-60 wasted minutes per window. The hypothesis is testable from existing iter records (already have wall-clock numbers).
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.ts` (the `renderSystemPromptOverlay` brief composer), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/spawn-plan.test.ts` (assert the new clause + env-escape behaviour).

- [ ] `docs-operator-troubleshooting-prompt-too-long` — add a troubleshooting doc covering the `claude --print` prompt-too-long failure on heavy `~/.claude/` setups

  - **ID**: docs-operator-troubleshooting-prompt-too-long
  - **Tags**: documentation, operator-experience, claude-code, p2, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: On machines with a heavy `~/.claude/` ecosystem (many skills + plugins + agents + rules accumulated over months — e.g. 92MB plugin marketplaces, 1GB session history, 74KB+ CLAUDE.md), `claude --print` exits 1 with "Prompt is too long" before processing any user input — the auto-loaded system prompt alone exceeds the model context. The documented escape hatches (`--bare`, `--setting-sources project,local`, `--disable-slash-commands`) have caveats: `--bare` disables OAuth/keychain auth (requires `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`), and `--setting-sources` doesn't prune plugin/skill auto-loading. Today's MINSKY workaround is `MINSKY_WORKER=devin` (PR #4bb10f9 on `feat/devin-as-headless-worker`). Adding `docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` with the symptom → root cause → workarounds → verification path saves the next operator the ~30 min I spent diagnosing.
  - **Success**: `docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` exists with a section "`claude --print` fails with 'Prompt is too long'" containing: (a) symptom screenshot/text, (b) root cause explanation (auto-loaded context overflow), (c) workarounds (devin worker recommended path; `--bare` + API key alternative), (d) verification (`echo 'reply OK' | claude --print` should exit 0 with response "OK"). README.md "Troubleshooting" section links to this doc. `pnpm lint:md` (markdownlint) exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: If the doc adds confusion (operators try `--bare` without API key + report new "Not logged in" failures, OR they expect the doc to fix their setup automatically), trim the workarounds list to just the devin-worker recommendation and link upstream to anthropic-claude-code's docs for the auth detail. Doc is reference, not a tool.
  - **Measurement**: `test -f docs/operator-troubleshooting.md && grep -c "Prompt is too long" docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` ≥ 1 AND `grep -c "operator-troubleshooting" README.md` ≥ 1.
  - **Anchor**: Wickham, *R Packages*, 2nd ed., Ch. 10 §"Other markdown files" — README + troubleshooting are siblings; troubleshooting captures the "I hit this error, what now?" path that the README's happy-path doesn't cover. Diátaxis framework (<https://diataxis.fr/>) §"How-to guides" agrees.
  - **Why**: 2026-05-16 12:51-13:30Z (example-service-api session) — operator hit "Prompt is too long" on first minsky run. Investigation took ~30 min before discovering `--bare` won't work without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. A doc would have shortened this to 5 min.
  - **Files**: `docs/operator-troubleshooting.md` (new), `README.md` (one-line link in "Troubleshooting" or equivalent section).

- [ ] `host-loop-operator-branch-pin-with-auto-stash` — minsky-run should checkout MINSKY_OPERATOR_BRANCH (with auto-stash) before each picker invocation so the operator's curated task queue is always visible

  - **ID**: host-loop-operator-branch-pin-with-auto-stash
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, host-loop, branch-strategy, p2, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: Devin's per-task spawn checks out `feat/<task-id>` (branched from `default_branch`/master) and leaves HEAD there at end of iteration. The picker (next tick) reads TASKS.md from THAT branch — which lacks any Rule #9-substrate reformats the operator committed only on their working branch. Result: picker finds 0 compliant tasks → seed-on-empty fires → CTO audit composes new tasks → minsky exits empty-queue → external watchdog respawns. Adding a `MINSKY_OPERATOR_BRANCH=feat/<branch>` env (or `--operator-branch <name>` CLI flag) that `git switch <name>` (with `git stash push -m "minsky auto-stash"` first to handle dirty WIP) BEFORE each picker call eliminates the orphaned-reformat-branch problem. Today an external watchdog at `/tmp/minsky-example-service-api-devin/watchdog.sh` does this — but it's a workaround layer that should be built in.
  - **Success**: After landing the flag, a synthetic test sets `MINSKY_OPERATOR_BRANCH=feat/test-operator`, spawns minsky-run in a fixture repo where `master` has 0 Hypothesis tasks but `feat/test-operator` has 3, runs 1 iteration: the picker selects from the 3 (not the 0). When the iteration completes and HEAD ends on `feat/<task-id>`, the NEXT picker tick `git switch feat/test-operator` succeeds (auto-stashing any worker WIP) and the picker again sees the 3 tasks. `pnpm test` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: If auto-stash captures content that confuses the next devin worker (the new HEAD has a stash-branch hint and devin tries to "fix" the conflict), switch to using a dedicated worktree at `.minsky/worktrees/operator-branch/` for picker-only reads — the worker still operates in the main checkout, but the picker reads TASKS.md from the pinned worktree. More complex but isolates picker from worker.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c "MINSKY_OPERATOR_BRANCH" novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` ≥ 1 (env wiring landed) AND `pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts -t "operator branch" --reporter=verbose 2>&1 | grep -i "pass" | head -3` (≥ 1 passing test case).
  - **Anchor**: Cohn, *Pro Git*, 2nd ed. (2014), Ch. 7 §"Stashing and Cleaning" — auto-stash on branch switch is the canonical multi-task workspace pattern (`git switch --autostash` since 2.20). Convention is to pin the curated branch + auto-stash before transitions, not to fight branch state with an external supervisor.
  - **Why**: Observed on example-service-api host 2026-05-16 20:17Z onward: my Rule #9 reformat branch (`feat/minsky-task-rule9-fields-PROJ-720` with 8-12 compliant tasks) was inaccessible to the picker every time devin's per-task spawn left HEAD on `feat/lma-middleware-...` / `feat/example-model-use-merge-...` (with 0 reformats). External watchdog's HEAD-restore step (added 21:45Z) hit `git switch` failures 2x because of uncommitted WIP. Built-in pin + auto-stash collapses this to one config var.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (CLI + env), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (pre-pick hook), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts` (tests), `docs/operator-branch-pin.md` (new operator-facing doc).

- [ ] `runner-scope-leak-soft-mode` — relax scope-leak verdict from "kills iteration" to "warns + continues" because devin's natural fix scope is broader than the task's **Files**: declaration

  - **ID**: runner-scope-leak-soft-mode
  - **Tags**: cross-repo-runner, runner, verdict-tuning, p2, surfaced-by-example-service-api-monitoring
  - **Detected-by**: devin-session-2026-05-16-monitoring
  - **Detected-at**: 2026-05-16T22:30Z
  - **Hypothesis**: `runLive` in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts:166-169` returns `verdict: scope-leak` when the worker writes files outside the task's `**Files**:` / `**Touches**:` declaration, which `runOneIteration` treats as a fatal verdict that halts the loop. Devin's natural fix-it style spans related files (helpers, callers, integration tests, docs) that the original task author didn't anticipate. On the `lma-middleware-canonical-header-overhaul` task (2026-05-16 21:32Z + 21:35Z), devin scope-leaked TWICE in a row — each time discarded — because the task's `**Files**:` listed only 2 files but the coherent fix touched 12 (matching what PR #614 had already shipped). Adding `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=warn|hard` (default `warn`) — emit a structured WARN log with the offending paths but DON'T kill the iteration, just record the verdict as `validated-scope-warn` — lets the operator review post-hoc without losing the work.
  - **Success**: After landing the mode flag, a synthetic test with `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=warn` and a worker that writes 1 in-scope + 2 out-of-scope files: iteration verdict is `validated-scope-warn`, the iteration record's `scopeLeakPaths` field contains the 2 out-of-scope paths, AND the runner emits a WARN log line that an operator dashboard could pick up. With `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=hard` (legacy default override), behavior matches today's scope-leak → halt.
  - **Pivot**: If `warn` mode lets devin "wander" into unrelated files (sample 20 iterations post-change; if ≥3 show file modifications uncorrelated with the task's stated intent — operator's subjective judgment), revert to `hard` default and instead invest in a "scope autocomplete" linter that pre-expands `**Files**:` to include adjacent test/doc files when the task author writes only the implementation file.
  - **Measurement**: `cd /Users/fivanishche/apps/tooling/minsky && pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.test.ts -t "scope-leak-mode" --reporter=verbose 2>&1 | tail -20` (≥ 2 new passing test cases — warn-mode happy path + hard-mode legacy).
  - **Anchor**: Cockburn, *Crystal Clear*, 2004, Ch. 3 §"Vertical Slices" — vertical-slice features inherently span multiple files (impl + test + doc + caller updates). A `**Files**:` field that lists only the impl file forces a horizontal-slice fiction onto a vertical-slice reality. The published spec-kit pattern (which minsky inherits via Rule #9) explicitly assumes a vertical slice; the runner's scope-leak verdict should align.
  - **Why**: 4 iterations across 2 distinct tasks (lma-middleware-canonical + example-model-use-merge) hit scope-leak in 2h on example-service-api host. Each one wasted 3-15 min of devin compute and forced a watchdog respawn. The scope-leak verdict was fighting devin's instinct instead of informing it.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts` (scope-leak detection at line 166-169), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (line 282 — the `if (outcome.verdict === "scope-leak") return "scope-leak"` early-exit), `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (env wiring).

  - **Tags**: p2, parser, scope-leak, observed-in-fleet
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.test.ts`
  - **Hypothesis**: `parseFilesField` (`runner.ts:251-258`) regex `^\s*-\s*\*\*Files\*\*:\s*(.+)$/m` only matches inline content on the same line as `**Files**:`. Many real-world TASKS.md files (including the `example-service-plugin` repo's, which we ran against on 2026-05-16) use a nested-bullet form: `**Files**:` on its own line, then a blank line, then indented `-`-prefixed `path/x.ts` items. For these blocks the regex misses, `allowedPaths` returns empty, `detectScopeLeak` short-circuits (`runner.ts:94 — if (allowedPaths.length === 0) return []`), and the scope-leak gate is silently bypassed. Pre-registration: post-fix, when `parseFilesField` finds `**Files**:` with no inline content but a nested-bullet list follows, it walks forward collecting indented `-`-prefixed items (stripping leading backticks + trailing `(new)` / `(modified)` annotations) and returns them as `allowedPaths`. Across the 7-task example-service-plugin TASKS.md, `extractAllowedPathsFromTaskBlock` returns ≥1 path for every P0/P1 task instead of 0 for all of them — closes the silently-fail-open hole that companion `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=warn|hard` only papered over.
  - **Success**: against an unmodified `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/TASKS.md`, `extractAllowedPathsFromTaskBlock` returns ≥1 path for every P0/P1 task (today: 0 for every task in that file) AND existing 4 inline-form paired tests still pass unchanged.
  - **Details**: (a) Extend `parseFilesField` to detect the multi-line form: when the inline regex misses but a `**Files**:` line exists, scan forward up to 20 lines, collecting any line that matches `^\s+-\s+(.+)$` until indent drops below `**Files**` indent + 2 OR a blank line is followed by a non-list line. (b) Per-path: strip leading/trailing backticks, strip a trailing space-prefixed `(new)` / `(modified)` / `(no change)` annotation, trim. (c) Three new paired tests in `runner.test.ts`: (i) multi-line-3-paths-no-annotations; (ii) multi-line-with-annotations; (iii) mixed-inline-AND-multi-line (defensive — prefer the inline form if both present). (d) Symmetric support in `parseTouchesField`. (e) Top-of-function JSDoc documents both supported shapes with examples.
  - **Verification**: paired tests above. Live re-run against `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/TASKS.md` (pre-flatten — see companion task in that repo's PR #291): `node --input-type=module -e 'import {parseTasksMd, extractAllowedPathsFromTaskBlock} from "./novel/cross-repo-runner/dist/index.js"; ...'` returns ≥1 path for every P0/P1 task. Existing 4 inline-form paired tests at `runner.test.ts:239-280` still pass unchanged.
  - **Measurement**: against `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/TASKS.md` (pre-flatten), `extractAllowedPathsFromTaskBlock` per-task path-count median ≥ 2 (today: 0 for every task in that file). Companion measurement after both fixes ship: rolling 7d of iterations marked `scope-leak` AND with `pr_url != null` drops to 0 (today's number for the example-service-plugin host alone: 4).
  - **Pivot**: if multi-line parsing introduces false-positive globs (picks up file names from `**Details**:` continuation prose) more than 1 in 30 task blocks, narrow the multi-line scanner to ONLY accept lines that look like file paths (start with a known prefix `src/`, `tests/`, `scripts/`, `docs/`, OR end with a known extension `.ts | .tsx | .js | .mjs | .json | .md`). If THAT still produces false positives, retire the multi-line support and document the inline-only constraint with a tasks-md-lint rule that warns at author time (see agentbrew `tasks-md-files-field-inline-format-lint` companion task).
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `parseFilesField` accepts the multi-line nested-bullet form (3 new paired tests); (2) `parseTouchesField` accepts the same form (1 new paired test); (3) JSDoc on both functions documents the two supported shapes; (4) live re-run against unmodified `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/TASKS.md` returns non-empty allowedPaths for every P0/P1 task; (5) existing 4 inline-form paired tests still pass unchanged.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run — scope-leak detection silently fail-open on every task because the multi-line form was the convention there. The tasks.md spec at <https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md/blob/main/spec.md> doesn't prescribe a single form for `**Files**:`, so the parser must accept both. Companion task in example-service-plugin (`flatten-files-field-for-minsky-scope-leak`, #291) flattens that repo's format as a workaround; this task fixes the parser so future hosts following the spec's multi-line convention don't need workarounds.
  - **Risk**: low. The change is additive (existing inline parsing unchanged), bounded (max 20 lines of forward-scan), and gated by paired tests. Failure mode is the Pivot's false-positive case, mitigated by the prefix/extension filter.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin autonomous run — iteration 1 of `parameterize-auth-posture-probe` marked `scope-leak` with no actual scope leak. Iteration record at `~/apps/example-service/example-service-plugin/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/parameterize-auth-posture-probe.jsonl`. Sibling task `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=warn|hard` (the P2 above) covers the verdict-recovery path; this task covers the parser-correctness path.

- [ ] `minsky-stop-host-filter` — `minsky stop` should accept `--host <dir>` to limit SIGTERM to a single host instead of every minsky-run on the machine

  - **ID**: minsky-stop-host-filter
  - **Tags**: p2, cli, multi-tenant-safety, observed-in-fleet
  - **Touches**: `bin/minsky` (the bash shim), `bin/minsky.test.mjs` (new — first paired test for the shim)
  - **Hypothesis**: Today `minsky stop` (defined in `bin/minsky` ~line 70-78) runs `pkill -TERM -f "cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run"` — it SIGTERMs every `minsky-run` on the host regardless of which host repo each is driving. When two operators (or one operator running two minsky-runs in parallel — e.g. plugin + api at the same machine) co-exist, calling `minsky stop` to clean up one of them sends SIGTERM to BOTH. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky stop` accepts an optional `--host <dir>` filter. `minsky stop --host /Users/.../example-service-plugin` SIGTERMs only the minsky-run whose argv contains the matching `--host`. `minsky stop` with no flag stays the existing global behavior but prints a pre-kill banner listing every host that's about to be stopped + a 3s grace period to abort with Ctrl-C.
  - **Success**: `pgrep -c "cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run"` after `minsky stop --host /tmp/host-a` equals pre-stop count minus 1 (only the matching host killed), AND `minsky stop` without flag prints the host-list banner and sleeps 3s before killing.
  - **Details**: (a) Extend the `bin/minsky` bash shim's `case` block for `stop` to parse `--host <dir>` via shift+positional. (b) When `--host` is set: `pgrep -f "cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.*--host $RESOLVED_DIR"` (use `realpath` so relative paths still match absolute-path argv). Loop: kill each matched pid; report `sent SIGTERM to pid $P (host=$RESOLVED_DIR)`. (c) When `--host` not set: pre-list every match's argv via `ps`, sleep 3s (unless `MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1`) before sending the kill so the operator can Ctrl-C to abort. (d) `minsky stop --help` documents both shapes. (e) Two paired tests in a new `bin/minsky.test.mjs`: --host filter case (mock pgrep returns two processes, verify only the matching one is killed) and no-filter case (verify both are killed + the warning banner is printed). Note: the existing minsky shim is bash and isn't unit-tested today; this is the first paired test for it.
  - **Verification**: paired tests above. Live integration: in two terminals, run `minsky --host /tmp/host-a` and `minsky --host /tmp/host-b` (both bootstrapped). In a third terminal: `minsky stop --host /tmp/host-a` — terminal A exits cleanly, terminal B keeps running.
  - **Measurement**: `pgrep -c "cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run"` after `minsky stop --host /tmp/host-a` equals pre-stop count minus 1. Without the filter (today's behavior): equals 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the `--host` matcher produces false matches (kills a minsky-run whose host path is a SUBSTRING of the argument) more than 1 in 50 invocations, switch to exact-match via `realpath` + explicit `--host="$DIR"` argv pattern instead of substring `pgrep -f`. If false matches persist after that, retire the filter and revert to today's global behavior with the warning banner as the only safety.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `minsky stop --host <dir>` SIGTERMs only the matching minsky-run; (2) `minsky stop` (no flag) prints the host-list banner and sleeps 3s before killing; (3) `MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1 minsky stop` skips the banner; (4) two paired tests pass; (5) `minsky stop --help` documents both shapes.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run — operator (this session) had two minsky-runs concurrent (plugin + api on the other session), needed to restart only the plugin one without killing the api one. Today's `minsky stop` would have killed both. Workaround used: direct PID kill via `kill -TERM <pid>`. Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — `minsky stop --host` is the operator's per-host kill switch; today's global stop crosses the wrong boundary). Hyrum's Law: the host-filter capability is exactly what multi-operator machines need.
  - **Risk**: low. Bash-shim-only change, additive (no flag preserves today's behavior + adds the safety banner), gated by the first paired test for the shim.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin autonomous run — supervisor log at `/tmp/minsky-example-service-plugin/supervisor.log` documents that the operator had to be careful about `minsky stop` interaction with the other session's API minsky-run. Workaround was direct PID kill; this task documents the right CLI shape.

- [ ] `demo-pr-generator` — `minsky run --target=<oss-repo> --output-mode=pr-only` produces a single high-quality demo PR per OSS repo (the funnel)
  - **ID**: demo-pr-generator
  - **Tags**: vision, business, growth, distribution, cross-repo
  - **Estimate**: 2w (compose-from-existing-primitives; no new architecture)
  - **Hypothesis**: A bot that opens a *single* meaningful PR against a target OSS repo — analytics dashboard wired up, chaos table written, rule-#9 hypothesis attached, OTEL spans on hotpaths — is *demonstrably* useful in a way most dev tools aren't. Maintainers see the work, not the marketing. The demo PR is the funnel; converted maintainers either self-host the CLI (free, runs the supervisor on their machine) or sign up for the cloud tier (Minsky-hosted supervisor running 24/7 against their repo). Conversion-rate hypothesis: the click-through from "demo PR opened" to "README badge / cloud signup" is ≥5% across 100 OSS repos in the first quarter (compare to Dependabot's ~30% adoption rate post-acquisition; we're solving a different problem than dep updates so conservative target). Composes from existing primitives: `@minsky/cross-repo-runner` v0 (host-targeting), `@minsky/handoff-spec` (the PR body shape), `@minsky/sidecar-bootstrap` (the per-repo `.minsky/` scaffold). v1 = the operator hand-picks 10 OSS repos and runs the generator manually; v2 = an autonomous discovery layer (GH search by stars + language + activity recency) feeds the queue. **Important constraint**: defaults to *one PR per repo per quarter, opt-in via README badge*, NOT bulk drive-by — Dependabot fatigue is the failure mode.
  - **Details**: (a) New CLI mode `--output-mode=pr-only` on `@minsky/cross-repo-runner` — instead of writing to the host's `.minsky/experiment-store/`, it runs one supervisor iteration in a temporary worktree, then opens a PR via `gh pr create` against the target's default branch with the changes + a templated body (analytics summary + chaos table + rule-#9 self-grade). (b) Templated PR body in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-template.ts` (pure function — diff stats + signal counts + signup CTA). (c) Idempotency: the generator checks for an existing `[minsky-demo]` label / PR via `gh pr list --label minsky-demo` before opening; never duplicates. (d) Frequency cap: refuses to open if the last `[minsky-demo]` PR on the repo is <90d old. (e) Rate limit: refuses to open if more than N PRs in a 24h window globally (anti-spam). (f) Opt-in surface: target repo's README must contain `<!-- minsky-demo: opt-in -->` OR a maintainer must invite the bot via `@minsky-bot demo` on an issue. v1 leans toward the opt-in side; the autonomous discovery layer is v2. (g) Per the user's vision (2026-05-04): the PR body invites the maintainer to add Minsky to the repo for ongoing supervision — the CTA is the conversion event.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-mode.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-template.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-mode.test.ts` (new — paired tests for idempotency + rate-limit + opt-in checks), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (mode documented), vision.md § Pattern conformance index (new row).
  - **Verification**: 6 paired tests (idempotent / opt-out-respected / rate-limit-honored / template-renders / dry-run-prints-diff / live-mode-opens-PR-against-fixture-repo); manual test run against `fyodoriv/minsky-demo-target` (operator-owned scratch repo) succeeds with one PR opened.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --repo <target> --label minsky-demo --json createdAt,state,reactions --jq '. | length'` ≥ 1 after the manual run. Conversion tracking: `gh pr list ... --jq '[.[] | select(.reactions.totalCount > 0)] | length / length * 100'` ≥ 5 % across 10 manually-targeted OSS repos in 90 days post-launch.
  - **Pivot**: if maintainer reception is hostile (≥1 spam complaint per 10 PRs over the first 30 PRs, or any GH abuse-report), pivot from autonomous-PR to invitation-only. The opt-in `<!-- minsky-demo: opt-in -->` README marker becomes mandatory; we never open PRs unprompted. The discovery-driven v2 stays shelved.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) demo PR opened against an operator-controlled fixture repo with a well-formed body; (2) idempotency + rate-limit + opt-in checks covered by paired tests; (3) PR body's CTA links to the cloud-signup landing page (separate task — the landing page itself is the next thing); (4) manual run against ≥3 real OSS repos to validate maintainer reaction (operator gates between runs). NOT in v1: autonomous discovery, scheduling, billing.
  - **Anchor**: vision (user brief 2026-05-04 — "demo PR is the trojan horse for the cloud tier"); rule #1 (composes existing primitives, doesn't reinvent); rule #12 (this task IS the new scope; pre-registered above); Cialdini *Influence*, 1984 (reciprocity — a maintainer who received a useful PR is more likely to engage); Raymond *The Cathedral and the Bazaar*, 1999 (community-as-distribution — every adopted PR is a distribution surface). Anti-pattern anchor: Dependabot's drive-by PR fatigue at scale (`https://github.com/dependabot/dependabot-core` issue-tracker around 2021-2022) — the per-repo-per-quarter cap is the explicit response.
  - **Risk**: high. The blast radius extends to GitHub's abuse-detection systems and to OSS maintainer goodwill, neither of which we control. Mitigation: hard rate-limit + opt-in default + Pivot threshold tied to the first abuse signal. Stop the autonomous loop if any maintainer asks once.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user vision conversation — "what if minsky is so successful at improving itself that one day it starts choosing open source repos, analyzing them 1 by 1 and writing for each a meaningful improvement pr that demonstrates the whole functionality of minsky".

- [ ] `paid-tier-features-skeleton` — implement the cloud-supervisor + cross-repo-benchmark + invariant-catalog features (free tier for now; paywall comes later)
  - **ID**: paid-tier-features-skeleton
  - **Tags**: vision, business, revenue, cross-repo, observability
  - **Estimate**: 4-6w (three orthogonal features; each its own sub-task)
  - **Hypothesis**: The free CLI does ~95 % of the value (you self-host the supervisor on your machine; it runs the loop against your repo). The cloud tier has to deliver value the local CLI structurally cannot — specifically: **(a) cross-repo benchmarking** (your dashboard's p95 latency vs the median Minsky-managed Node service; only Minsky-cloud has the cross-cohort data), **(b) shared invariant catalog** (the 47 invariants we've collectively detected across 10k repos, available as a one-line `import` in your `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`; only Minsky-cloud aggregates these), **(c) compliance attestation** (a Minsky-signed quarterly proof that your repo passes the constitutional rule-set; auditors / customers want a signed PDF, not a "trust me bro" README claim). Free vs paid axis is **who hosts the supervisor**, not amount of work — paid = Minsky-cloud runs the supervisor 24/7 + provides (a)/(b)/(c); free = you run the supervisor locally + see your own data only. **Importantly for now**: implement all three features but make them free until we have ≥3 paying-customer demand signals (an unscientific qualitative gate; the alternative — guess at price first — is the vanity-metric trap rule #9 forbids). Paywall task is a separate later task.
  - **Details**: Three sub-tasks, each its own task block to be added when this one ships:
    - **`cloud-supervisor-mode`** — Minsky-cloud-hosted supervisor: a containerised tick-loop that mounts a target repo via the GH App, runs the loop, files PRs through the bot account. Reuses 100 % of the existing `@minsky/tick-loop` daemon — only the I/O boundary changes (GH App auth instead of local fs; OTEL endpoint points at our cloud aggregator). Pivot if cold-start cost per repo per loop iteration exceeds Anthropic's per-call cost by >10× — at that point the cloud tier is unprofitable even free.
    - **`cross-repo-benchmark-aggregator`** — Minsky-cloud aggregates anonymised metric snapshots from every consenting repo (the 10 success metrics already shipped); per-repo dashboard adds a "you vs the cohort median" overlay. Schema: `{repoId, metricId, valueAtTimestamp[], cohortHash}`, retention 90d, opt-in only. Pivot if cohort sizes stay <100 across all metric IDs — without ≥100 repos per cohort the benchmark is statistically meaningless and we should pivot to industry-standard reference (Forsgren/DORA 2018 numbers) instead.
    - **`shared-invariant-catalog`** — `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` accepts `--catalog=cloud` and pulls additional invariants from `cloud.minsky.dev/invariants`. Each invariant ships with its own paired test + suggestedFix (same shape as the seed invariants in PR #156). v1 = read-only catalog; v2 = community contributions via PR (rule #1: "push upstream" is the discipline). Pivot if catalog growth stalls (<5 new invariants per quarter from non-operator sources) — at that point the catalog is just our seed list and the cloud value disappears.
  - **Files** (skeleton; sub-tasks fill in): `novel/cloud-supervisor/` (new package), `novel/cross-repo-benchmark/` (new package), `novel/shared-invariant-catalog/` (new package), `cloud/` (new directory — deployment manifests for the cloud bits), vision.md § Pattern conformance index (3 new rows).
  - **Verification**: each sub-task ships its own paired tests + chaos table; the umbrella task is "all three sub-tasks shipped + integration test that the cloud bits don't break the local CLI" (a `MINSKY_CLOUD=disabled` env var disables every cloud probe — the local CLI must work identically when set).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-cloud-disabled.mjs` (new lint) — verifies the CLI runs successfully with `MINSKY_CLOUD=disabled` and produces output identical to the no-cloud-bits baseline. Failing this lint blocks merge of any sub-task PR. Cohort-size measurement: the benchmark aggregator's tests assert ≥100 synthetic repos in the cohort fixture; production-stage measurement is `cloud.minsky.dev/admin/cohort-sizes` (lives in the cloud-deploy task).
  - **Pivot**: if after 6 weeks none of the three features show *any* user-visible value in dogfood (operator's own eyes), pivot to picking just one feature. The candidate ordering by leverage: (1) shared-invariant-catalog (compounds with each new invariant authored), (2) cross-repo-benchmark (compounds with each new repo enrolled), (3) cloud-supervisor (highest infra cost, lowest moat — anyone can run a supervisor in a container).
  - **Acceptance**: three sub-tasks shipped behind `MINSKY_CLOUD={enabled,disabled}` flag; default is `disabled` (free tier ships the local CLI with cloud probes off); `MINSKY_CLOUD=enabled` requires the cloud account (deferred — billing is `paywall-and-billing` task). All three features land as code, all are free during the demand-discovery period.
  - **Anchor**: vision (user brief 2026-05-04 — "free vs paid axis is amount of work"; revised in this conversation to "free vs paid axis is who hosts the supervisor"); rule #2 (every cloud feature behind a Strategy seam — the local CLI keeps working with cloud disabled); rule #9 (each sub-task carries its own hypothesis + measurement + pivot — entered when it's filed); Hamilton, *Foundations of Software Engineering*, 1986 (the rule "build the substrate first, charge for it later" — every paid SaaS we know followed this pattern); Christensen, *The Innovator's Dilemma*, 1997 (a free CLI that does 95 % of the value is the disruptor against tools that bundle the supervisor and the analytics together).
  - **Risk**: high. Cloud infrastructure is a step-change in operational complexity (auth, billing-once-paywall-lands, multi-tenant data isolation, OTEL ingestion at scale). Mitigation: ship one sub-task at a time, each behind its own `MINSKY_CLOUD_<feature>=disabled` flag, with the local CLI remaining the first-class default. The Pivot threshold (none of three features shows value in dogfood) is the hard gate.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user vision conversation — "Minsky has free tier and paid tier" + my 2026-05-04 reply identifying the moat axes (cross-repo benchmarking / shared invariant catalog / compliance attestation). User's response: "let's add tasks for paid features (temporarily free for now, let's implement the features first)". This task block operationalises that.

- [ ] `omc-tasksmd-bridge-v1-watcher` — reverse-sync + filesystem watcher for the OMC ↔ tasks.md bridge
  - **ID**: omc-tasksmd-bridge-v1-watcher
  - **Tags**: novel, bridge, follow-up, dormant-until-crdt-story
  - **Estimate**: 1–2w (CRDT story + watcher + reverse-sync)
  - **Hypothesis**: Once a CRDT story is sketched for OMC's optimistic-concurrency `version` field (`src/team/state/tasks.ts:90`), a chokidar / `fs.watch`-driven reverse path (tasks.md edits → OMC `claim` / `complete` calls) can propagate a claim in either direction within 1 scheduler iteration without lost-update collisions across 100 random concurrent-edit trials. v0 (read-only) shipped as `@minsky/omc-tasksmd-bridge`; this task closes the deferred half of the original `omc-tasksmd-bridge-v0` Acceptance ("claim propagation in either direction").
  - **Details**: Add `OmcWriter.{claim,complete,update}` mirroring OMC's persisted shape; integrate `chokidar` (or `fs.watch` if portable enough) on both `<repoRoot>/.omc/state/team/**/tasks/*.json` and `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md`; resolve conflicts via OMC's `version` field (compare-and-set). Lossy fields documented in `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/README.md` § "Lossy projection" must be addressed before reverse-sync is safe — either widen the tasks.md spec or extend the bridge to a sidecar JSON.
  - **Files**: `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/{watcher,writer,conflict-resolution}.{ts,test.ts}`, `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/README.md` (chaos-table additions for the new failure modes)
  - **Verification**: Round-trip property test (random TASKS.md ↔ OMC trials, ≥95 % pass at 100 trials); claim-propagation E2E (claim in either side observed in the other within 1 scheduler iteration).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/round-trip.property.test.ts` exits 0 with ≥95 passed property cases; `pnpm vitest run novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/claim-propagation.e2e.test.ts` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the CRDT story for `version` cannot reach lost-update-free convergence at 100 random concurrent-edit trials (≥1 lost update detected), the reverse path isn't viable; pivot to a *write-throttled* reverse direction (single-writer assumption, scheduler-iteration-rate-limited) and document the asymmetry, OR escalate `omc-tasksmd-issue` to push tasks.md adoption upstream so the bridge can retire entirely.
  - **Acceptance**: Round-trip property test passes ≥95 / 100 trials; claim propagates in either direction within 1 scheduler iteration; bridge published as v1.
  - **Anchor**: Shapiro et al., "Conflict-free Replicated Data Types", *SSS* 2011 (the CRDT story this task waits on); Helland, "Life beyond Distributed Transactions", *CIDR* 2007 (the bridge's eventual-consistency frame); Hewitt 1973 (TASKS.md as the message store).
  - **Risk**: OMC adopts tasks.md upstream before this task lands → the bridge retires entirely (the Goldratt TOC win); track via `omc-tasksmd-issue` in TASKS.md.

  - **ID**: review-q3-2026
  - **Tags**: governance
  - **Estimate**: 1d (when due)
  - **Hypothesis**: A quarterly scan of all 14 deps + 5 novel layers surfaces ≥1 dependency whose situation changed materially since the last review (new alternative, deprecation, security advisory) — enough to justify the review's standing existence per rule #1. *Additionally*, the quarterly review reads `validated-learnings.md` and the experiment-tracker verdict log, summarising the calibration of rule #9's predictions (predicted Δ vs observed Δ by hypothesis category) — closing rule #9's quarterly automation layer for any window the MAPE-K loop has not yet covered.
  - **Details**: Per vision.md principle 1, scan all 14 deps and 5 novel layers; reconsider choices. Append to `research.md` "Quarterly review log". **Rule-#9 quarterly-layer scope:** the review's standing checklist now includes (a) total experiments tracked, (b) % `validated`/`regressed`/`inconclusive`, (c) calibration table (mean predicted Δ vs mean observed Δ, grouped by hypothesis category — feature / refactor / bugfix / docs), (d) rule-#9 amendment proposals if any category is systematically miscalibrated.
  - **Verification**: `research.md` has a 2026-Q3 entry under "Quarterly review log" with one line per dep + one line per novel layer
  - **Measurement**: `awk '/^### 2026-Q3/{flag=1; next} /^### /{flag=0} flag' research.md | grep -c '^- '` ≥ 19 (14 deps + 5 novel layers); follow-up tasks filed for any dep flagged → `gh issue list --label dep-review --search '2026-Q3'` recorded in the entry.
  - **Pivot**: if 3 consecutive quarterly reviews surface zero material changes, drop the cadence to semi-annual; if a review surfaces ≥3 material changes, raise to bi-monthly until the rate normalises.
  - **Acceptance**: research.md updated with findings; any dep changes filed as separate P1/P2 tasks
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent the wheel); Fowler, *Refactoring*, 1999 (review cadence as a refactoring discipline at the architectural scale).
  - **Risk**: Skipped if no calendar reminder set. Add a calendar event before this task is due.

- [ ] `lighthouse-self-hosted-runner-pivot` — Next-tier pivot if Lighthouse Mobile 0.85 also proves flaky on GH-hosted runners
  - **ID**: lighthouse-self-hosted-runner-pivot
  - **Tags**: infra, testing, ci, pivot-followup, dashboard-web
  - **Estimate**: 4h
  - **Hypothesis**: Following the 2026-05-04 threshold-pivot from 0.9 → 0.85 (`.github/workflows/lighthouse.yml`, vision.md row 58), the new `≥0.85` Lighthouse Mobile gate is *expected* to be stable on GH-hosted runners — the original observations (0.83 / 0.89) sat 1–2 percentage points below 0.9, so a 5-point drop to 0.85 should swallow the noise. If 0.85 also proves flaky (≥2 false-positive failures per 10 runs at the new threshold over 30 days), the residual variance is structural to the GH-hosted runner (CPU steal, neighbour-VM contention) rather than a tunable threshold property — the only remaining lever is to move Lighthouse to a self-hosted runner with predictable CPU. Same precedent as `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner`.
