Document the runner provisioning needs (predictable CPU, no nested virtualization, Chromium-installable). Coordinate with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` to share infrastructure if both fire — one self-hosted runner can host both jobs. If self-hosted is rejected on cost / ownership grounds, retire the Lighthouse gate entirely and rely on the dashboard-web LoC-cap + chaos-table audits as the residual `dashboard-web-v0` performance proxy — document the asymmetry as a declared deviation in vision.md row 58 and `novel/dashboard-web/README.md`.
  - **Files**: `.github/workflows/lighthouse.yml`, `novel/dashboard-web/README.md`, `vision.md` (row 58 update), `docs/self-hosted-runner.md` (shared with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if it has also fired)
  - **Verification**: 3 consecutive PRs see `lighthouse-mobile` land as `success` on the self-hosted runner with a Lighthouse score reproducibly above 0.85 (variance band ≤ 0.03 across the 3 runs).
  - **Measurement**: `gh run list --workflow lighthouse.yml --branch main --limit 10 --json conclusion --jq '[.[] | .conclusion] | map(select(. == "success")) | length' >= 8` (≥80 % success rate over the last 10 runs after the move) AND a paired `gh run download` + `jq '.categories.performance.score' lighthouse.json` over the same 10 reports shows max−min ≤ 0.03.
  - **Pivot**: if self-hosted-runner maintenance burden exceeds the empirical signal value (e.g., the runner needs >1 manual intervention per quarter), or if 0.85 proves stable for 30 consecutive days *without* the move (the trigger never fires), retire this dormant task — it is a scout entry, not a commitment. If self-hosted is moved to but the variance remains >0.03 across runs, the gate is non-deterministic at root and should be retired entirely (dashboard-web's LoC-cap + chaos-table audits become the residual proxy).
  - **Acceptance**: This task fires *only* if the new 0.85 threshold sees ≥2 false-positive failures per 10 runs sustained over 30 days. Otherwise it remains a dormant scout entry.
  - **Anchor**: rule #9 (vision.md § 9 — pre-registered pivot threshold; this is the next-tier pivot pre-registered in the original `dashboard-web-lighthouse-ci` task); Forsgren, Humble, Kim, *Accelerate*, IT Revolution Press, 2018 (DORA test-reliability — a CI gate that doesn't run reliably teaches the team to ignore failure); Wilkie, "RED Method", *USENIX SREcon EMEA* 2018 (the duration component is the user-perceived metric — moving runners preserves the metric's semantic); Munafò et al., *Nature Human Behaviour* 1, 0021, 2017 (pre-registration — the next-tier pivot was committed *before* the 0.85 threshold's behaviour was observed, in the same PR that lowered the threshold).
  - **Risk**: Self-hosted runners introduce supply-chain risk (a compromised runner can leak secrets). Mitigation: scope the runner to public-repo / non-secret jobs only; share infrastructure with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if both fire (cost amortisation); standard GH guidance (Forsgren 2018 § DORA prerequisites; rule #7).

- [ ] `next-task-scope-to-jira-ticket` — `/next-task` should accept a Jira-key argument to pin one-shot bug fixes
  - **ID**: next-task-scope-to-jira-ticket
  - **Tags**: skill, ergonomics, one-shot, surfaced-by-fresh-install
  - **Estimate**: 1h
  - **Hypothesis**: `/next-task` today picks the highest-priority unblocked task across all `~/apps/*/TASKS.md` (per README "queue mode"). For one-shot operator workflows ("ship the fix for PROJ-840 and stop"), the operator must either temp-edit TASKS.md to bump priority or run the work outside `/next-task`. Letting `/next-task <ticket-or-id>` (e.g. `/next-task PROJ-840` or `/next-task proj-840-slash-command-labels`) pin the queue to that one task — claim it, ship it, exit instead of looping — closes the "I just want this one bug shipped" path without weakening the default queue-mode loop. The match is a substring search across either the `**ID**:` field or the task title (the title contains the Jira key for tickets).
  - **Details**: Update `.claude/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` (or wherever the skill lives — confirm via `tasks install` if the auto-install flag works in 0.7.x; per setup.sh comment 295-297, 0.7.0 install is broken, so the skill is hand-committed). Add a `<args>` parser: empty → existing queue-mode; non-empty → grep TASKS.md for the literal arg (Jira-key OR kebab-case ID), claim that single task, work it, exit on completion *without* re-entering the loop. Keep the existing audit-cascade behaviour as the default.
  - **Files**: `.claude/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` (or the equivalent path post-`tasks install` shipping), a small unit test that simulates the arg-parsing path.
  - **Verification**: `/next-task PROJ-840` claims `proj-840-slash-command-labels` from `~/apps/example-capabilities-3/TASKS.md` (via the title-match path), ships the PR, exits — does NOT proceed to the next P1.
  - **Measurement**: An integration shell-script that seeds `~/apps/test-fixture/TASKS.md` with two tasks, calls the skill driver with the second task's Jira-key as arg, and asserts the first task remains unclaimed at end-of-run (`grep -c '@' TASKS.md` == 1).
  - **Pivot**: if Jira-key matching collides with kebab-id matching often enough that operators get the wrong task (≥1 mis-claim per 10 invocations), restrict matching to `**ID**:` field only and require operators to use kebab-case IDs (PROJ-840 → `proj-840-slash-command-labels`).
  - **Acceptance**: One-shot mode works from the README's documented path; queue-mode unchanged when arg is empty; collision behaviour documented.
  - **Anchor**: Cooper, *About Face: The Essentials of Interaction Design*, 4th ed., Wiley, 2014 (modal vs modeless interfaces — the same affordance carrying both queue-mode and one-shot mode is modeless, and modeless wins when the user's intent is unambiguous from the arg); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `/next-task` already exists, the change is one optional arg).
  - **Risk**: low. Default behaviour (no arg) is preserved; the new arg path is opt-in.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 — operator wanted to one-shot PROJ-840 in example-capabilities-3 and had to reason about how `/next-task` would interact with example-capabilities-3's pre-existing P0/P1 queue (deep engagement-onboarding work that takes priority by ID order). Workaround: filed the bug as P1 above the larger refactors, but a Jira-key arg would have been cleaner.

- [ ] `cross-repo-host-daemon-loop` — `minsky-run --loop` keeps invoking `runLive` against the host's TASKS.md until the queue is empty or SIGTERM (@devin)
  - **ID**: cross-repo-host-daemon-loop
  - **Tags**: novel, cross-repo, runner, daemon, host
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/**`, `experiments/cross-repo-host-daemon-loop-*.yaml`
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: After `cross-repo-runner-v1-live-spawn` (PR #489) ships the one-shot `--live` path, the next gap is the *continuous* path — a host operator wants `minsky-run --host ~/apps/example-service --live --loop` to keep ticking through the host's rule-#9-compliant queue without manual re-invocation. Reusing `runLive` per-iteration (rule #1) + a thin tick scheduler in the same CLI (rule #6 — let-it-crash AT the iteration boundary, not the loop) yields the smallest viable host-side supervisor without unwinding `runDaemon`'s minsky-on-itself substrate. The launchd / systemd unit templates for host mode are deferred to a follow-up — the in-process loop is the functional surface this task closes against; the operator substrate is the next slice.
  - **Details**: (a) Add `--loop` flag to `bin/minsky-run.mjs`; mutually compatible with `--live`. (b) Pure `pickHostTask(tasksMd): ParsedTask | null` that selects the first rule-#9-compliant `P0` or `P1` task (all 5 fields present). (c) Pure `runHostLoop({ hostRoot, config, maxIterations, tickIntervalMs, spawn, git, globMatchesPath, sleep, now, signal }): Promise<LoopResult>` orchestrator. (d) CLI wires `runHostLoop` with the real `ProcessSpawnStrategy` + `execFile("git", …)` probe. (e) SIGTERM handler aborts the in-flight iteration via AbortSignal; pending iterations exit cleanly. (f) Stop conditions: `--max-iterations=N` cap, OR `pickHostTask` returns null (empty queue), OR SIGTERM. Default `--max-iterations=Infinity`, `--tick-interval-ms=300000` (5 min, mirrors `runDaemon`'s production cadence).
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` + `host-loop.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/task-finder.ts` (extend with `pickHostTask`), `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (add `--loop` + `--max-iterations` + `--tick-interval-ms` flags), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (new "`--loop` (continuous host-mode iteration)" section), `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/proj-840-shape.test.ts` (extend with `--loop --max-iterations=1` dry-run path).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner` exits 0 with the new `host-loop.test.ts` + the extended integration test passing. `minsky-run --host <bootstrapped-host> --loop --max-iterations=1 --tick-interval-ms=0` (no `--live`) drains one task block from the host's queue and exits 0.
  - **Measurement**: `bash -c 'cd <repo> && npx vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json | jq -e ".numPassedTests >= 170 and .numFailedTests == 0"'` exits 0 (today: 82; new tests + integration extension push the floor above 170).
  - **Pivot**: if `runHostLoop` proves to need budget-guard / paused-sentinel / claim-file integration to be useful (every host-mode invocation immediately hits a state the host operator can't observe), retire `--loop` as a v0 surface and ship the full `runDaemon`-equivalent in a follow-up that imports the seams from `@minsky/tick-loop`. The pure `runHostLoop` survives as substrate.
  - **Acceptance**: `--loop` flag exists; SIGTERM aborts in-flight iteration cleanly (no zombie spawn); empty-queue exit is verdict `no-task` not error; integration test covers the loop's stop conditions.
  - **Anchor**: Liu & Layland, "Scheduling Algorithms for Multiprogramming in a Hard Real-Time Environment", *Journal of the ACM* 20 (1), 1973 (periodic-task scheduling — `tickIntervalMs` is the period, `runLive` is the task; same anchor `runDaemon` cites for the minsky-on-itself surface); Armstrong, *Programming Erlang*, Pragmatic Bookshelf, 2007 (let-it-crash AT the iteration boundary; SIGTERM is the supervisor's normal-exit signal); rule #1 (don't reinvent — reuse `runLive` from PR #489); rule #6 (vision.md § 6 — stay alive across process death; the loop's stop conditions ARE the let-it-crash surface).
  - **Risk**: low. The loop is in-process; SIGTERM cleanly exits. No supervisor unit yet — operator runs in foreground (or under their own nohup/screen). Long-running ergonomics (auto-restart on crash, log rotation) are explicit follow-ups, not v0 promises.

- [ ] `cross-repo-cto-audit-host-mode` — `minsky-run --cto-audit` proposes rule-#9-compliant task blocks for the host repo so the daemon keeps going past empty-queue (@devin)
  - **ID**: cross-repo-cto-audit-host-mode
  - **Tags**: novel, cross-repo, runner, cto-audit, autonomic
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/**`, `experiments/cross-repo-cto-audit-host-mode-*.yaml`
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: Slices A (PR #489) and B (PR #490) close the cross-repo *execution* surface — a host operator can drain a rule-#9-compliant queue continuously. The remaining gap is the *generation* surface: when the queue empties, the daemon stops. The minsky-on-itself loop (`@minsky/tick-loop`) solves this with `post-task-cto-audit.ts` — a second `claude --print` invocation after each shipped iteration that proposes 1–3 follow-up task blocks. This task ships the cross-repo equivalent: a `runHostCtoAudit` pure orchestrator that builds a CTO-mode brief tailored to the host repo (reads TASKS.md / README / recent git log) and spawns Claude to write rule-#9-compliant task block(s) into the host's queue. Wired via a new `--cto-audit` CLI flag that fires the audit (a) after every `validated`-verdict iteration in `--loop` mode, AND (b) on `empty-queue` so the loop self-seeds instead of exiting. Same `SpawnLike` seam (rule #1 reuse — `ProcessSpawnStrategy`), new brief, new lifecycle hook.
  - **Details**: (a) Add `src/host-cto-audit.ts` with pure `buildHostCtoBrief(opts): string` (CTO-mode prompt asking for 1–3 rule-#9 task blocks for the host) + `shouldRunHostCtoAudit(opts): { fire: boolean; reason: string }` gate (filters no-op verdicts + the audit's own audit). (b) Add `runHostCtoAudit({ hostRoot, config, reason, spawn }): Promise<{ outcome: "ran" | "skipped"; details: ... }>` that builds the brief, spawns claude via the same `SpawnLike` interface, and records the result in `experiment-store/cross-repo-cto/<date>.jsonl`. (c) Wire into `runHostLoop`: new `--cto-audit` flag adds a post-iteration `cto-audit` hook + flips `empty-queue` from a stop reason to a "seed and continue" path (operator opt-in only — default is the slice B stop-on-empty behaviour). (d) Iteration records carry the new verdict `cto-audit-completed` so `gh pr list --label minsky:cto-audit` on the host can be counted toward the pre-registered metric.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-cto-audit.ts` + `host-cto-audit.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts` (extend with optional `ctoAudit` seam), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts` (add tests for the seam dispatch), `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs` (add `--cto-audit` flag), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (new `--cto-audit (auto-task-generation)` section), `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/proj-840-shape.test.ts` (extend with `--cto-audit` dry-run path).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner` exits 0 with the new `host-cto-audit.test.ts` + extended `host-loop.test.ts` + extended integration test passing. `minsky-run --host <bootstrapped-host> --loop --cto-audit --max-iterations=2 --tick-interval-ms=0` (no `--live`) fires the CTO audit after the dry-run iteration AND on empty queue.
  - **Measurement**: `bash -c 'cd <repo> && npx vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json | jq -e ".numPassedTests >= 125 and .numFailedTests == 0"'` exits 0 (today: 105; new tests push the floor above 125).
  - **Pivot**: if the CTO audit's prompt produces vanity-metric task blocks (counts-go-up tasks per Ries 2011) or fabricates non-existent file paths > 20 % of the time on real hosts, retire the auto-fire from `--loop` and keep `--cto-audit` as a one-shot operator surface only (`minsky-run --host <dir> --cto-audit-once`). The pure `runHostCtoAudit` survives. Decision boundary: < 0.40 of audit-PRs ship (`merged / opened`) over the trailing 60 days against ≥ 5 distinct host repos.
  - **Acceptance**: `--cto-audit` flag exists; post-iteration audit fires only on `validated` verdicts (skips no-op / scope-leak / spawn-failed); empty-queue with `--cto-audit` seeds new tasks instead of exiting (with `--max-iterations` still bounding the total); the spawned CTO brief explicitly asks for rule-#9 substrate AND refuses to file vanity-metric tasks (same anti-vanity discipline as `@minsky/tick-loop`'s `post-task-cto-audit`).
  - **Anchor**: Kephart, J. O., Chess, D. M., "The Vision of Autonomic Computing", *IEEE Computer* 36 (1), 2003 (MAPE-K Plan phase — the CTO audit IS the Plan phase of cross-repo work, generating new work items the Execute phase ships); Goldratt, E. M., *The Goal: A Process of Ongoing Improvement*, North River Press, 1984 (Theory of Constraints — the CTO audit identifies the highest-leverage next constraint to lift; ISBN 978-0884271956); Ries, E., *The Lean Startup*, Crown Business, 2011 (validated-learning discipline — the audit's success metric is *PRs that ship*, not PRs that get filed; ISBN 978-0307887894); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `post-task-cto-audit.ts` from `@minsky/tick-loop` is the existing primitive; this task adapts its shape for host mode without forking the brief logic); rule #9 (vision.md § 9 — every proposed task block carries the rule-9 substrate or it's not eligible).
  - **Risk**: medium. The CTO audit's brief is LLM-driven, so brief drift is the operational risk. Mitigation: the same prompt template as `@minsky/tick-loop`'s CTO audit (with host-mode parameterisation), and the gate predicate filters bad outputs before they hit the host's queue. The cap-1-per-iteration contract (lockfile in `experiment-store/cross-repo-cto/`) prevents runaway audit fanout.

- [ ] `minsky-status-iteration-digest` — `minsky status` shows iteration counts, success/fail rates, and avg duration in addition to running processes
  - **ID**: minsky-status-iteration-digest
  - **Tags**: p2, observer, cli, ergonomics, cross-repo
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: Today `minsky status` is a thin `pgrep` wrapper — it prints PIDs + command lines for running `minsky-run` processes, or "no running minsky-run on this host". For an unattended loop running for hours across multiple hosts the operator wants the *rollup*: how many iterations have run, how many shipped vs failed vs hit rate-limit, average wall-clock per iteration, last 5 iterations with verdict icons. The data already exists — `runHostLoop` and `runHostWalker` write iteration records to `.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl` per host. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky status` from a hosts-dir reads every `experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl` under the workspace, aggregates into the digest, and prints it under the existing pgrep output. The proof: an 8h loop run against `~/apps/example-service` (3 hosts, 191 expected iterations) produces a one-screen digest that the operator can eyeball without `cat`-ing jsonl files.
  - **Details**: (a) New pure `aggregateIterationRecords(records: IterationRecord[]): DigestSummary` in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/iteration-record.ts` (rule #2 — pure aggregation; the I/O is the file walker). `DigestSummary` carries `totalIterations`, `successful`, `failed`, `rateLimited`, `avgDurationMs`, `lastFiveIterations: Array<{ ts, host, taskId, verdict, durationMs }>`. (b) New I/O helper `readWorkspaceIterations(workspaceRoot: string, fs: FsLike): IterationRecord[]` that walks subdirs under `<root>/*/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl` (single-host: just `<root>/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl`). (c) Extend `bin/minsky`'s `status` subcommand: after the existing `pgrep` block, detect cwd as hosts-dir (cwd-detect) and print the aggregated digest. (d) New `--json` flag on `minsky status` so the digest can feed dashboards / Watchcomplications. (e) Co-located test for `aggregateIterationRecords` covering: empty input → all-zeros; mixed verdicts → correct counts; rate-limited fallback (`exitCode != 0 AND notes ~= /rate.?limit/i`) classified separately from "failed".
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/iteration-record.ts` (extend with `aggregateIterationRecords` + `DigestSummary` types), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/iteration-record.test.ts` (paired tests for the aggregator), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/status-walker.ts` + `status-walker.test.ts` (new — the fs walker), `bin/minsky` (extend `status` subcommand), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` ("Status digest" section under Usage).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the pure aggregator (≥6 cases). Integration: synthetic jsonl fixtures in `test/integration/status-digest-*.jsonl`, assert the digest matches expected counts + last-5 ordering. Manual: run `minsky --no-live --max-iterations=3` against a fixture workspace, then `minsky status` shows 3 iterations + correct verdicts.
  - **Measurement**: `bash -c 'cd <repo> && pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json | jq -e ".numPassedTests >= 180 and .numFailedTests == 0"'` exits 0 (today: 174; new tests push above 180). Bonus probe: `bash -c 'cd <fixture> && minsky status --json | jq -e ".totalIterations == 3"'` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the digest's stat-aggregation cost exceeds 100 ms on a workspace with 1000 iterations (large multi-host fleet), pivot to writing a `digest.json` snapshot per host after each iteration so `minsky status` is O(1) per host rather than O(N) per iteration. The pure aggregator survives as the snapshot writer.
  - **Acceptance**: `minsky status` from a hosts-dir prints both the running-processes section AND the iteration digest; `--json` flag emits machine-readable form; paired tests cover empty / mixed / rate-limited cases; `pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner` passes.
  - **Anchor**: rule #4 (everything visible — the dashboard counts as observability; if you have to `cat` jsonl files, it isn't visible); Boyd's OODA loop, *A Discourse on Winning and Losing*, 1976 (Observe phase — the operator needs the data summarised before they can Orient); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `aggregateIterationRecords` is pure data manipulation, no new framework). Surfaced-by: porting `~/apps/example-service/minsky-loop-status.mjs` (the predecessor script, 8h-loop-validated) into minsky proper after PR #500 (single-quote scalar fix) made the runner usable in that workspace.
  - **Risk**: low. Read-only over jsonl files we already write. The digest itself is a pure transformation — easy to test, easy to evolve.

- [ ] `minsky-push-stuck-branches` — `minsky push-stuck` finds local-only branches matching the loop's branch-prefix and pushes them + opens draft PRs
  - **ID**: minsky-push-stuck-branches
  - **Tags**: p2, observer, cli, recovery, cross-repo
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: When the loop runs claude with `--dangerously-skip-permissions`, the spawn should be able to `git push` and `gh pr create`. In practice some sandbox configurations (older claude versions, certain `MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1` paths, network hiccups) leave a branch committed locally but never pushed — and the operator has no good way to find and ship that work after the fact. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky push-stuck` walks every bootstrapped host under cwd, lists local branches matching the host's `branch_prefix` (from `.minsky/repo.yaml`) that (a) have no `origin/<branch>` ref AND (b) have ≥1 commit ahead of `default_branch`, and pushes them + opens a draft PR. The proof: after a flaky 8h loop where ~5% of iterations had unpushed work, running `minsky push-stuck` recovers all of them in one shot.
  - **Details**: (a) Pure `findStuckBranches(repoState: RepoState, config: RepoConfig): StuckBranch[]` in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/push-stuck.ts` — input is a synthetic snapshot of `git branch --format='%(refname:short)'` + per-branch ahead-count, output is the subset that's stuck. Strategy seam — production wires `execFile("git", ...)`; tests inject the snapshot. (b) Pure `buildDraftPrBody(commitMessage: string, hostInfo: { repo: string; commitFooter: string }): string` that renders the PR body with attribution footer and a `Why this is needed` section derived from the commit subject. (c) I/O wrapper `pushStuckBranches({ hostRoot, fs, git, gh, log }): Promise<{ pushed: number; prsOpened: number; skipped: number }>`. (d) New `bin/minsky` subcommand `push-stuck` (peer of `status` / `stop`): cwd-detect → single-host (push from cwd) or multi-host (iterate over bootstrapped subdirs). (e) Idempotent: branches that already have a remote ref or an open PR are skipped silently. (f) Operator escape hatch: `--dry-run` lists what would be pushed without actually pushing.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/push-stuck.ts` + `push-stuck.test.ts` (pure decisions for find + body-build), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/push-stuck-io.ts` + `push-stuck-io.test.ts` (the I/O wrapper with injected seams), `bin/minsky` (extend with `push-stuck` subcommand + `--dry-run`), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` ("Recovery: `push-stuck`" section).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `findStuckBranches` (≥5 cases: nothing-stuck, single-stuck, multi-stuck, already-has-PR-skipped, not-matching-prefix-skipped). Paired tests for `buildDraftPrBody` (footer present, commit subject reflected). Integration: a fixture worktree with 2 local-only branches matching the prefix; `pushStuckBranches` against an injected `gh`/`git` returns `pushed=2, prsOpened=2`. Live verify: run against `~/apps/example-service` from the 8h loop's tail state and recover any genuinely-stuck branches.
  - **Measurement**: `bash -c 'cd <repo> && pnpm exec vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner --reporter=json | jq -e ".numPassedTests >= 190 and .numFailedTests == 0"'` exits 0 (today: 174; this + `minsky-status-iteration-digest` push above 190). Manual: after running `minsky push-stuck` against `~/apps/example-service` on a known-stuck-branches state, `gh pr list --state open --author "@me"` shows exactly the recovered PRs.
  - **Pivot**: if `findStuckBranches` produces false positives (pushes legitimate work-in-progress branches the operator didn't want shipped), pivot to opt-in: only push branches that end in a configurable suffix (e.g., `-AUTO-${LOOP_SESSION}`). The pure decision function survives; just tighten the predicate.
  - **Acceptance**: `minsky push-stuck` subcommand exists; `--dry-run` is supported; paired tests cover the 5+ cases; idempotency: re-running has zero side effects when nothing is stuck; the recovered PRs carry the canonical attribution footer.
  - **Anchor**: rule #6 (vision.md § 6 — stay alive across process death; the loop crashing mid-push is exactly the failure mode this recovers from); Perrow, *Normal Accidents*, 1984 (recovery procedures must exist for the failure modes the system is known to produce); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `git push` + `gh pr create` are existing primitives; this is the composition). Surfaced-by: porting `~/apps/example-service/minsky-loop-pusher.mjs` (the predecessor script, 8h-loop-validated) into minsky proper after PR #500 (single-quote scalar fix) made the runner usable in that workspace.
  - **Risk**: low-medium. The push step IS destructive (creates a remote branch + PR under the operator's identity), but the predicate is restrictive (matches branch_prefix + ahead-count > 0 + no existing remote) and the escape hatch (`--dry-run`) is the default first invocation pattern. The PR body's `Why needed` is derived from the commit, not invented — the operator can always close the PR if it's not wanted.

  - **ID**: bosun-extraction-sweep-followups
  - **Tags**: p3, meta, bosun-extraction, audit, deferred
  - **Touches**: `TASKS.md`, `/tmp/bosun-to-minsky-extraction-analysis.md`
  - **Hypothesis**: the 2026-05-12 bosun-extraction sweep filed 4 high-confidence P2 tasks (`daemon-multi-provider-rate-limit-detector`, `cross-repo-runner-per-repo-project-memory`, `daemon-cross-vendor-reviewer-bias-prevention`, `daemon-pr-feedback-extraction`) and identified 7 anti-recs (do not port). It also identified 5+ smaller patterns that are *possibly* extractable but where the value vs. effort ratio was unclear at filing time. Pre-registration: by 2026-09-01 (3 months out), run a one-shot revisit pass against these candidates with grounded data from the daemon's own observability (do the failure modes these patterns guard against actually occur in minsky's logs over the 90-day window?). For each candidate, the verdict is either (a) file as P2/P3 with a real rule-#9 substrate, (b) close as not-worth-the-effort with a one-line rationale + the data that justified the close, or (c) defer for another quarter. The deferred candidates are listed in the Details. Verdict deferred because cross-repo-runner today uses a single host directory. Revisit if `cross-repo-runner-multi-host-mode` (not yet filed) becomes a real need: this is the right shape for the brief assembly.
    - **`bosun-self-update-service-port`** — `~/apps/experiments/bosun/orchestrator/server/src/service/selfUpdateService.ts` (auto-restart on `origin/main` changes; recency-window-aware). Verdict deferred because minsky's daemon currently restarts via the launchd/systemd supervisor (which already handles binary updates on the supervisor's own restart cycle). Revisit if the supervisor's restart cycle proves too coarse (e.g. takes > 5min to pick up a critical fix) over 30d of operations.
    - **`bosun-additional-dirs-shape-for-cross-repo-runner`** — same source. Different framing — even without multi-host mode, the host runner could read up to N additional doc-only files from the host (e.g. `experiments/*.yaml`, `docs/*.md`) to enrich the brief.
  - **Files**: `TASKS.md` (this meta-task block updated as candidates resolve), `/tmp/bosun-to-minsky-extraction-analysis.md` (the persistent artefact of the 2026-05-12 analysis).

- [ ] `host-loop-soft-failure-continue-mode` — autonomous loop should keep iterating on `spawn-failed` instead of halting, so a single bad iteration doesn't end an N-hour fleet run

  - **ID**: host-loop-soft-failure-continue-mode
  - **Tags**: p3, host-loop, autonomous-fleet, observed-in-fleet
  - **Touches**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/host-loop.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/bin/minsky-run.mjs`
  - **Hypothesis**: `runOneIteration` in `host-loop.ts:282-283` returns `"spawn-failed"` to the parent loop the moment any iteration's verdict is `spawn-failed`, and the parent `runHostLoop` (host-loop.ts:201) immediately exits. For a long-running autonomous fleet (the operator launched `minsky --host` with a 6h budget), a single bad iteration shouldn't terminate the loop — it should record + advance to the next task. The operator's 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run hit this 7 times across 9 iterations; each time the supervisor had to relaunch minsky. Pre-registration: post-fix, `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES=continue` (env override) makes `runHostLoop` treat `spawn-failed` like `validated` for loop-continuation purposes — the iteration record still says `spawn-failed`, but the loop sleeps `tickIntervalMs` and continues to next iteration. Default behavior (no env) preserves today's halt-on-failure semantics. With soft-failures-continue enabled and a 6h budget, the operator can launch one `minsky --host` invocation and walk away instead of running a supervisor sidecar.
  - **Success**: with `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES=continue` and a 5-iteration target, a force-SIGTERMed iteration 2 still produces 5 iteration records (1 spawn-failed + 4 validated). Today's halt-on-failure default still produces only 2 records.
  - **Details**: (a) Extend `RunHostLoopOpts` with `softFailures?: "continue" | "halt"` (default `"halt"`). (b) In `runOneIteration` (host-loop.ts:282-283), branch on `opts.softFailures`: if `"halt"`, return `"spawn-failed"` (today's behavior); if `"continue"`, return `undefined` so the loop proceeds to `sleepBetween`. (c) Mirror for `scope-leak` if companion `MINSKY_SCOPE_LEAK_MODE=warn` is also enabled (defer cross-flag interaction to a follow-up if it gets complicated). (d) `minsky-run.mjs` plumbs `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES=continue` into `runHostLoop({ softFailures: "continue" })`. (e) Three new paired tests in `host-loop.test.ts`: soft-failures-continue-on-spawn-failed (loop continues), soft-failures-halt-on-spawn-failed (today's behavior preserved), soft-failures-continue-still-respects-max-iterations.
  - **Verification**: paired tests above. Live integration on the example-service-plugin host with `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES=continue`: launch `minsky --host <dir> --max-iterations=5`, inject a `spawn-failed` on iteration 2 (force-SIGTERM the worker), assert iterations 3-5 all run to completion AND the iteration store has 5 records (1 spawn-failed + 4 validated). Without the flag (today's behavior): assert iteration 2 is the last record.
  - **Measurement**: `cat <hostRoot>/.minsky/experiment-store/cross-repo/*.jsonl | wc -l` for a 6h fleet run with N=10 target iterations: ≥ 9 records (1 failure tolerated) with the flag enabled; today: 1 record (loop exits on first failure).
  - **Pivot**: if `continue` mode masks a real problem (e.g. the same task fails 5 times in a row because of an unfixable env issue, and minsky never tells the operator), add a sibling env var `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES_MAX_CONSECUTIVE=3` that exits the loop after N consecutive failures on the same task (not N total failures — N back-to-back on the same task-id). If that's still insufficient, demote `continue` to opt-in-per-task via a `**Soft-failure**: continue` field on each task block.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `runHostLoop` accepts `softFailures: "continue" | "halt"` (default `"halt"`); (2) `MINSKY_SOFT_FAILURES=continue` env plumbed; (3) three paired tests pass; (4) live integration on example-service-plugin completes 5 iterations with 1 failure injected mid-loop.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin run — supervisor at `/tmp/minsky-example-service-plugin/supervisor.sh` had to restart minsky after every spawn-failed because of the halt-on-failure semantics. 9 iterations took 4h wall-clock to ship 7 PRs because of the restart overhead. With soft-failures-continue, the same workload would run in one `minsky --host` invocation. Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — a single iteration's failure is the WORKER's boundary, not the LOOP's; the loop should be resilient to individual failures). Beyer et al., *SRE*, 2016, Ch. 6 (degraded-but-running > failed-and-stopped for long-lived workloads).
  - **Risk**: low. Opt-in via env var (default behavior unchanged), gated by paired tests. Failure mode is the masked-real-problem case in the Pivot, mitigated by the `MAX_CONSECUTIVE` safety.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-16 example-service-plugin autonomous run — see `/tmp/minsky-example-service-plugin/supervisor.log` for the restart-every-iteration pattern that this task obviates.
